Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the ancients "cure contuse," and it is that you do behind to the patient who has this disease the hairs that he may have on his forehead, then make him III cuts on his forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the cuts be as II doe all down the forehead in swallowing down juice up to the nose, and the other II as II ribs by above the paper, and beware of the incision of the arteries that are as II sides by above the paper; and remove your hand from the continuation of the II jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of III doe across joined; and have ready a piece of sponge and much of cloths his to wipe away the blood, then put the spatula sharp of II parts of which here is the form: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is behind the temple up to the second incision; and flay all the core which is between the II cuts at all the syfac which is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision up to the other second, and then extract with this spatula. 
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument called "cultellaire" into the first fissure, it is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other. 
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	Place the sharp side towards the flesh burned at the core and the blunt side toward the bone and push it until it reaches the middle fissure. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cut all the vessels that descend from the head to those points so that the incision is continuous until it reaches what appears at the core and then do likewise in the middle fissure until the other end; then draw out the blood equally and press the area for the blood to be absorbed; then put a tent of old cotton into each fissure and place soft cloths soaked in wine, oil and alum on top and watch so that no boils appear; and on the third day untie the ligature and apply a large poultice of hot water, then cure it with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other remedies for curing wounds until it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	about the burning of the eyes 
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When some catarrh arises accustomedly, and you see the eyes swollen and small, and weaken the sight, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and when the head is full of pain, and the patient sneezes; then know by these accidents that those humors and this catarrh come forth from many veins, and the remedy which there is, if it is this. 
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you order the patient to lie on his back, then make a large incision along the forehead, and another two fingerbreadths wide from the first. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be down to the bone; and remove your hand from the nerves of the temples that move during chewing; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then insert between the two lips of the incision cotton wool soaked in linen threads; then bind over cloths moistened in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is removed, it is fitting that you rub the bone until a char begins to form, then cure it with drying agents, which cause charring. 
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flower, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster; and administer it in these wounds to draw flesh throughout. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	For the stuffing of ears 
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that is found in the ears is one of four things: either grains, or an animal, or a stone from a mine or similar things such as iron; or seeds, such as lentils, beans, peas; or flowing things such as water and easily removable things and similar things.  
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When there is a stone or another kind of thing in the ear that does not fit in the ear nor grow in it, put the ear in the sun.  
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then instill a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil, and then administer extraction; and make him sneeze forcefully, and stuff his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and hold the ear above. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times force comes by this treatment; and if it does not come by force, then administer extraction with delicate pincers, of which here is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes by force with the pincers, that is good; if not, then administer extraction with a delicate awl of small diameter; and if it does not come by this, then make a cane of iron and push the head of the cane or the perforation of the ear forcefully, and stuff that which is around the cane with soft wax so that the veins cannot enter with the cane; then pull forcefully, for many times force comes as we have said; and if it does not come by force in any manner, then take glue of which we take birds, and put some on any instrument suitable for this, and put a piece of cotton around; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull forcefully. 
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump from all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear in this way as for an abscess, chalazion, and spasm; and the manner of the incision is such that you make the patient healthy from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to the measure of his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear at the fat or place depending; and let the incision be as a crescent moon, until you come to the bone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin spatula according to this form: 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have cut it into many pieces; then extract it with delicate forceps and a syringe, as we have said, so that the extraction is clean. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In acute pain, when the head is in the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use a sneeze first, and to fill the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And he should lie on that same ear where the pain is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps strongly this way, it's good. 
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many pebbles according to the length of your thumb, light and warm them a little in the fire; then place one or two pebbles into the patient's ear and press down on it with your foot on the other side, and strike another pebble upon the one that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this from pebble to pebble until the pain subsides completely, and thus it will jump out entirely; and if you see that, take a piece of wire and heat one end in the fire, while the other end remains cool; then repeat with other wires until the pain subsides, as we have said for the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of a beast, if it is of small size, such as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that one can feel it, then use extraction with pincers; and this is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the removal of worms lodged in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the cure does not profit at all, then you must look at the ear in the sunlight: if there appears any worms, remove them with fine pincers, and if there are none, take a cane of which this is the form: 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the most delicate tip into the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then slowly withdraw the whole cane; do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, then cauterize around the canal with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out strongly as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the excision of worms, and you will find them where you treat distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, this is the form as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether it is of silver or iron, three holes below the small openings, and above covers for distilling; and to press the distillation inside the instrument of well-made iron for this purpose, and if you see take the razor and wrap around the point with cotton gently; then put your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the canal, and the canal is in the ear; then push the razor all the way into the cotton, and press your hand moderately so that the oil is distilled or reached from the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillations be slightly heated over the fire like this, we distill them in the ear; and keep it from being too cold, because the medicine would not be as good. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	For the softening of the ears 
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults by softening of a wound or a splinter inside the ear.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it comes to those that are hidden and cannot be seen, they cause grief and impede healing in many ways. 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind all plain, so that it does not scratch the ear; if the hair is from flesh or bone of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and pull lightly, as long as all the hairs are removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the hairs are embedded deep in the ear, then take a subtle razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then apply it to the flesh of the ear. 
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the hair that the patient feels pain in the ear, pierce lightly and be careful not to touch the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for no day until the wound is closed, or else take a tent and moisten it with rose water and powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then you should draw out the tent and insert another moistened with cerate made of rose oil and wax, as long as the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place them on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding which are found in treatises on distillations. 
de la char des papieres	of parchment  
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This athlull that comes in papers from the time they are moist and dry, it behoves you to extend them with tongs and pincers, and the end of a spatula from its roots; then put on the spot pulverized vitriol. 
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they do not come off, cauterize them gently with a lentil-shaped cautery, and cauterize again after the incision has healed; and often they are repaired, so that nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return. 
de la gresle	of gravel  
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come upon the eye things that resemble hail in their shape and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of moisture thick on the eye above and below; the work is such: take heed if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and this is a light thing to know; then make two wide incisions, then scrape lightly each part, then take it with pincers and cut it off. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it off, then pierce a bit the eye, it will not grieve anything to the patient; and if the fissure is large, then sew the gathering with stitches and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, then do not apply any force, for ointments will quickly restore it and bring forth flesh.  
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, then invert the eyelid and grasp the grandine with pincers, cut it off and press from one side to the other; and if the eyelid is loosened by the incision, it will not grieve anything; and when the grandine is cut off, wash the eye with clean warm water, and treat the place which brings forth flesh until the patient is healed. 
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes 
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is ingrained in cloths of paper on it, and this happens more to children than to adults, and grieves much their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears hasten to their eyes; and because of this they lie down on their faces then, and sleep upon them, and have their papers beneath their eyebrows moist so that it swells and its appearance has covered from the exinach which appears in the eye. 
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place at your fingers and feel the exinach between them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient puts his head in your lap; and then take a cloth of linen, and arrange a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity which contains exinach from each part, then put it on top of it; and press with your fingers on one side and the other so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a cut as wide, and no larger than the wound one makes at the opening of a vein; and make the skin perfect as you come to the exinach; and in several positions comes exinach from the cut, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.  
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then at once a piece of charred cloth between your fingers at the fire and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and see that you do not thrust into the fissure, lest you come to all the marrow up to the eye, lest you blind it. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the splinter does not appear at the beginning of the fissure, then widen the fissure slightly until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in water and vinegar, and place them on the spot, and bind with bandages. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are some men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then care for it until it is healed. 
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to the place, then treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed. 
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the paper 
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs from paper are added to those that are natural and aged, they harm them and cause various illnesses such as accustomed tears and softening of the paper, to such a degree that it causes their destruction; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by an aqueous medicine as described in the preceding chapter on cautery, and which is done either by incision and suture or by canes, as I will say.  
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper from the oil to your left hand; if it has converted, it is good; if not, insert a needle along all its threads above it; and let this be done at the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow next to these hairs, and draw the thread above the entire paper, and return it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the added hairs, along the whole spatula cutting, from the large tear to the small one; then extract the thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then trace on the paper a figure of an anchor, such as the leaf of myrtle, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you see raising the paper which is divided into all.  
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if one needs to take a large quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make all along the two lines that you have signed, and begin from the large tear to the small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the lancet into one of the two angles of the heart, then flay it all; then bring together the two lips with a stitch of a needle with all fine thread linen, and wipe away the blood, and air out the superfluity of the threads on the two eyebrows with anything sticky, if you see fit to do this; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the stitch and the threads until three or four days; then treat the wound without a stitch with drying and constricting things, for the paper will come alive at the healing of the wound and its joining, but the stitch is useless (as the ancients say), and this is work without fear; and if there is another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a shape that is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have said, with three lancets according to the shape which is here: 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take what is above, the small forces equally according to the form which is here: 
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the strength to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with thread, and put it in the shape; and put the other thread below the large tear, and the second thread below the small one, and assemble between your two hands the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have signed, as we have said, then assemble the two edges of the wound by suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and it sometimes happens that the hairs of the paper are converted: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial.  
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the canes is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and put the end inside according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of a span; and cut at two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on that which rises from the paper from the eye, and strain the two canes of the two parts formed; and leave it like that for several days, and the skin which grows strained will die and heal and bear, as long as it seeks by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, and if the cut has some strength, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is stitched, and if the paper is removed, and the hairs will no longer grow; and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works are such that you take a subtle needle, and you put a fine silk thread through it; then you assemble the hairs and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then arrange in the loop another subtle silk thread quickly, and tie the heads of the two threads; then put the patient's head on your lap; and let it be under the sun so that the work is clarified, for this is a subtle and small work, then put the needle all through the loop at the root of the hair closest to it, and make it pierce the paper quickly as you drag it over the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the loop, and put it in the loop, if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out all through the loop in the paper with the natural hair. 
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will treat the hair underneath all the way along the line that you have ordered, until the hair comes out freely through the holes above it and you can see it with the vision of your eye; then you will treat the hair and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows on top; and if the hairs are small, you will accompany one long horsehair, and let it grow with the one that you are leaving, until it is lengthened and then remove it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the eye 
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacratio" or corruption comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens through cutting of a wound, or by a cut or by a cautery, and by similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you cleave that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put inside linen tents, and bind it as long as it is healed; and it does not suit that you use in the cure of it things that dry and restrict. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the sickness returns worse than the first; but it works from things softening, such as fenugreek; and rose water or elderflower and flaxseed boiled, and ointments of diachylon melted in any of the oils, and it wraps a tent, and cures it with that. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure is that you give yourself in guard that it does not weld according to the form that it was before; and this work which we have said is nothing but dressings for this sickness, so that it does not return according to the form that it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes in the eye 
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness, which is below and is truly called "axacrati," and is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental cause comes from wounds and fissures and cautery and similar things; and the way to perform the procedure is that you take a needle, in which it has a double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct so that the threads come out at both sides of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above the entire needle, and cut it with a spatula two finger widths wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is proper, it is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make two fissures on either side within the paper; and let the sides of the two fissures be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make an angle so that when they are joined together, the shape is like the shape of a letter which has the Greek letter "I"; then remove that flesh, according to the amount its sides extend below, from what surrounds the paper, then join the two separated parts and sew them with a thread of wool; then apply the care that we have mentioned of softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a split or seam or cautery, it is fitting that you split a full split below the hairs of the papers, and according to what is said before; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare themselves from all their power how they make the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what suits them of work and instruments are in several dispositions. 
dou soudement de la papiere	Of paper reinforcement  
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture occurs in a bad manner so that the paper above is sewn with the white of an egg and cannot move or do its natural work, then it is fitting that you put the point of a razor below the paper and lift it up; and hold it with forceps, as long as you cut what is attached to a subtle spatula which is not too sharp nor too cutting so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula is too sharp nor bleeds the oil; and let your incision, by which you flay the assembled one, be lightly so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and heal all the assembled one, and sometimes do it in salt water and lift it with fresh water and colire; then put between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and put on the oil wool moistened abundantly with an egg; and after the third day use lukewarm colire and such things as are soothing until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	From the corner of the eye 
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: it is nervous and resembling hard bone; and another which is not nervous, but resembling white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and one thinks to pinch it, cannot be pinched by anyone; and both kinds begin near the large lachrymal gland, and grow little by little until they cover the whole vision and all the light and movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is such that the patient puts his head in good health, then he opens his eyes; and lifts the paper to his hand, then cuts the nail with pincers of small doubleure, and stretches it above; then takes a needle, and puts a hair of horse, or cow, or ox, and a strong thread; and doubles the point of the needle a little and sticks it into the nail, and pierces it through the whole needle, and ties the nail with a thread and stretches it above, and scrapes all the hair along the side of the nail which touches the prunele and the silk to the hair up to the head, then cuts off the remainder at the root near the tear gland with all subtle spatumile and small forces, and leaves the flesh natural or tear gland, so that by incision no body accustomedly comes from tears; and sometimes the nail is stretched only on the oncine alone, and to the thread, as we have said; then the scrape has been scraped at all the spatumile of which this is the form: 
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And make sure the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, and that the prune kernel is not pierced; and after the incision, put a piece of silk thread into the eye, and make a collar from silver, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it is healed. 
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this type of nail is cured by medicine; and it grows back as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, work on the eye of the patient, and take a light spatula with a sharp point according to this form: 
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail subtly, and if you see that it weakens a little and the razor presses it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of silver and a red collar of silk thread, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed. 
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing else is against you in the eye, such as an abscess, then milk it and first heal the hot abscess until it is cured, then start the work again as before, until it is cured. 
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the tear duct harms the eye greatly, suspend it with a thread and cover part of it but not all, so that no tears come; then instill red collyrium into the eye which is made from litharge. 
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the iris  
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men's eyes, flesh sometimes grows red and covers the iris, it shrinks on the eyelids and is cut off at the root; it looks like a rose made of balauste.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless it is necessary that you relieve the cure of each weak part by nature's way; and by accident, in work of iron; and do not put your hand in either of these works until you see that this limb can endure that work. 
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes 
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are red veins that are covered above the eye, and they take away from sight their work and weaken the eye every day. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary then at first that you look to see if the eye, in which the red vein is, is strong and there is no other illness except the red vein; then proceed in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on your knee, then suspend those veins at every ounce according to your skill, and let the ounces be subtle doubled according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be applied gradually throughout the body according to this form: 
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then one should press these veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after hour, until you see those outside veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to prick the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very eager in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, then instill into the eye green and red colirium to corrupt what remains from the ailment. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot remove all of it in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of soothing things for the pain of those veins, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and you are sure of hot abscesses, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:  
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye 
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it by cautery and by burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then it is necessary that you cut into the abscess where it must be drained, and remove all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed. 
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then you carve it with all the instruments of which this is the form; and it is called "aspre chief" and is made of hard iron at the head point, and is pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the spot of corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press with your hand a little while until you know that this corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the spot with drying medicines.  
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is soldered, and flesh grows, and the body of the fistula is soldered and remains thus for forty days, and it does not reopen nor become abscesses, and no evil accidents befall it, know that it is healed; if this is not the case, there is nothing else to do but to return the fistula to its opening according to this form:  and you uncover the bone a second time with an iron instrument and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take a drill bit according to this form, and let the head of the bit have three angles, and let the shaft be thinned down to the point as you see here. 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it upon the bone near the lachrymal bone, and withdraw your hand from the point a little, then turn the drill bit completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it, because the veins in this area are sensitive if he holds his hand on his nose; and then restore the site with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when flesh grows and the wound hardens, the matter will go to the nose; which is a lighter thing for the patient.  
de l’issue de l’oil	From the exit of the eye 
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens fully all around and there is no disturbance of the eyelid, nor any shrinking, then you should bind the patient; then he heals; then put cupping glasses or a leech on him without injuring to suck, then place a bandage made of gum arabic, aloe, incense and sarcocol upon the eye, and then strain the eye and apply plaster on bandages and cloths; and the manner of applying the cloths is that you should take cloths soft enough and double each one into four, and then put one on top of another according to the quantity which the eye needs; then strain it with a hard bandage over them and begin again the cupping glasses to suck without injuring; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the strained eye day and night, and if the bandages become loose, then you should tighten them greatly; then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see the eye recovering, it is good; if not; begin again the plaster, the cloths and the bandage and the cupping glasses until it is healed. 
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Where there is a tear in the woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, then it opens up, and there come forth papers as thin as a grain of resin, and is observable to see; then if you see it thus covered, the work is such that you put a needle into the root of the part below up to that above. Then put another needle where it has the double thread of the part near the tear; and make it pierce through, and leave the first needle according to its position; then take hold of the place of the double thread and tie one part of the cloth around it, and pull it tight, then remove the needle and put on the oil a linen cloth soaked in plenty of egg; and leave it until the threads grow with the cloth, then cure the oil with comforting things until the wound is healed; and at no time is the wound confined by the cloth each side of a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has a large appearance, pierce it with a fine spatula that comes perfectly from the oil, and correct the albuminous moisture and draw out the eye, and insert it quickly then; then extract it while it is healthy. 
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bowel of the oil 
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but bowel that is assembled in the oil, seeming like sharp descending, and it is not sharp; and the manner of the appearance of the work is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands in two parts, and move it until you see the bowel come up to your eyes; then let it be attached, and do not descend and be obscured the light, and see the patient the things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is sharp, and if the descending of the bowel is not level as we have said.  
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take a fine spatula and place it on the cornea, making an incision along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea, until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, pour into it sharp oil heated with honey, or sharp water where fenugreek has been boiled with honey, then let it be treated with another treatment until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	Of the sharp oil 
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the resemblances of sharps in the division, and what it takes to pierce; so work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is fitting that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, far from the light of the sun, and bind his healthy eye tightly; then place the paper with oil in your left hand if his eye is left, or in your right hand if his eye is right; then take in your right hand, if his eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if his eye is right; then put the point of the instrument below the cornea by the thickness of a hair in the white part of the eye towards the smaller tear duct; then push the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously, and turn your hand until it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that the "almagda" comes to the empty space; and it is fitting that the measure of the "almagda" path be at the perfection of the measure of the space which is from the prunele to the end of the blackness; and this is the cornea of the eye; if you see the bone in the paper due to the clarity of the cornea, then put the instrument up to where the sharp point is, then press it down one path after another.  
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the point is descending now, let the patient see it in front of him and the instrument in his eye. 
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a short rest, and if the point goes back up the second time, put force on it with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and it does not rise, extract the almond slightly while turning your hand little by little; then replace it with a point of silk thread, and lift the eye from within. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put oil dressings or moistened linen soaked in rose oil and egg yolk on the eye, and bind with the healthy eye.  
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Nowadays, we and those of our time put a common poultice with plenty of egg yolk on top.  
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have eyes too hard, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," which has this form: 
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle place, then it will bring almond, as we have said; and for the completion of the work prepare the patient with a doctor coming near him, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let it be devoid of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to its disposition until the third day; then untie it in that same dark house, and try its sight, and make it see some things, and then put the bond back on until the seventh day; and it is not fitting that you do this in the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is fitting that you relieve it, for the sharp pain rises quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess comes, that you untie the eye before the seventh day, and direct it to him who soothes abscesses; and when it is appeased, untie the sight and put on his face an orilliet to cover for a few days, and be then again in that dark house. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then he must leave the house little by little, and gradually return to his usual activities; and know that no disciples should interfere in this matter. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	One came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in some places they made a kind of almond paste, which we suck for sharp pain, but nevertheless I never saw any in our land, nor did I ever read of it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing. 
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almond paste, so that those who do not know them may recognize them: and they are made purely from starch: 
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the head is of the same subtlety, and the rear in three sharp angles. 
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh to the nose  
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or arise moles of various shapes, some of which appear like scorpions with many feet; and if there are such that have a mole tinged with a fiery color, and some that have a mole of a good color. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those cases of these cars which are soft and not hardened, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and work on his nostrils, and pour a little ointment on those cars, and pull them hard; then take what you can hold with a delicate scalpel on one side, as much as you know that this car is all removed. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that you cannot cut, work on it with all your subtle instruments lightly so that nothing remains; and if there is swelling or an abscess arises, make the incision as necessary; and if these are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them until the blood is dried up and all the cars are removed, then pour clean wine.  
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the wine works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not break through as it should, know that there is a car lodged in the bone above which the instruments cannot reach to cut: then it is necessary that you put a linen thread one finger thick, knotted by hand at each knot with a space of one finger or less between them; and have the patient hold the head of the thread in his nose at the top, and pull while smelling so that it comes through the nose into the mouth; and many times children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the end that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart as we are with those on a thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do what you know the new flesh has corrupted that body, then pull the thread, wipe away the blood, and wet the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back at the beginning just as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments have corroded everything that remains of the flesh; and then place a cane of lead on the wound for several days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, into which one pours oils and medicines. 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is of silver or steel, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and conduct it the same way; and if you see fit, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be filled for purging the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquid. 
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh take the birth 
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" is born at the head of a birth and grows and becomes large until it is visible; for this reason, you must cut it off at the beginning, and bone all strong, then put on it the cautery or burning medicine; if one delays cutting it while it is large, be careful if it is hard, dark red color, and poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchantered abscess. For when one cuts it, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not dark red in color, and you see that it can be all cut off, then empty the patient and cut without fear, and treat the place with drying and restraining things. 
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the birth is cut and sewn 
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
