It is therefore necessary when this happens to anyone, if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips at a suture, and then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you flay all the parts of their core until they bleed, then assemble the two lips at a suture, and remove it, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and put on the powders a piece of plaster of strong or another soldering plaster, and leave it until it dries by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is such that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have shown you. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips 
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	With bare hands, there often occur within the lips abscesses hard, appearing like grains of millet, both small and large; then you must turn back the lips and slit open each knot, and take them with pincers and cut into each part; then apply the place after incision with powdered vitriol, as long as the blood is stopped; and then a poultice of flaxseed, and treat the place with dry things until it is healed. 
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums 
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often arises upon the gums flesh overgrowing, which the ancients called "albulus"; so you must hold it with forceps and cut at its root, and let run the pus or blood; then apply to the place powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after incision, as often happens, cut it the second time and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting. 
des sordens	of the deaf 
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and citron and worm-eaten, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are stinking; so it behooves you to make the sick person sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your lap, and raise the teeth where the scabs appear, until there is nothing left; and thus do with the blackness and the greenness, and the jaundice and the other stains, until they are cleansed; and if one removes what is at the first reason, it is good; if not, one recommences on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments for raising, according to what the work shows, for the razor with which one raises sharp teeth has other forms than those with which one raises between the teeth; and these forms and others be prepared with you. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat a tooth for its pain that you delay as much as you can in extracting it, for this one must not do; for it is a very high substance until which one has no excuse for extracting it. 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to extract, it is necessary that you are certain of the aching tooth. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient and he thinks that it is in a good tooth and extracts the good tooth; and nevertheless the pain does not depart because of this, as long as the bad one remains, for we have often wanted to do this to these saints; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, then it is necessary that you flay around the tooth at its entire cusp very strongly in order to ward off the gums from all sides; then move it to your two fingers or with subtle forceps at the first blow and blow, as long as it is well loosened, then confirm it well with the forceps; and let the head of the patient be in your lap between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take any of these instruments and insert the tip into each side gently, and stir it as you did first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and chewed, it is necessary that you fill it with rags, where the holes are; and you must extract it subtly with forceps, so that it does not break when being extracted; and it is very wise to work around the gum to loosen the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and a part remains, and returns to the patient through the mischief of the root greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not do as ignorant healers often do, who by their haste and boldness break the tooth sometimes, and do not apply what we have said; but they bring about great sickness through the remaining roots or the broken tooth, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the place; and if that does not work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, with which one can pull teeth first, should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you extract the tooth; and these are the forms: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick shanks so that they do not bend when pulling, and be of well-made iron, and have teeth to hold the jaw. 
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth 
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after extraction, it is fitting that you put cotton moistened with butter on the place for one or two days. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the gums are softened, then you put the forceps which are called "algefri", of which the head resembles a bird's beak; and they are made inside like a file, and this is its form: 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is fitting that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say, a scraper, of which this is the form: 
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it must be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out because of this, it is good; if not, you help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come here after: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two handles, of which here is the form: 
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other ironworks that are in front in the manner of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tongs, of which here is the form: 
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument must be strong so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments which are not counted; and wise master-surgeons find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach an instrument because of the diversity of others, lest they break the chariot or other bones, or it rots, if he seeks the instruments that suit him, which I told you, and help yourself with gestures, of which here is the form: 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and strong to hold the bone so it does not escape, but can hold it and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, if you have all these instruments. 
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, it is necessary that you know if the density is born after the tooth and is not in its proper place, and cannot be smoothed or filed; then use a rasp; and if it sticks with the tooth, take this instrument of which this is the form, and resembles a small beak, and be made of sharp steel. 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the rasp pecks little by little in the hands for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then use a file of this shape:  
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth bit by bit in the hand every day lightly, so that it does not move until it comes out; then plane the end completely without any rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then you must file down the sharpness so that it is equal, so that it does not cut the tongue nor corrupt speech. 
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens 
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front loosens, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot press on what he is chewing without it coming loose, and you have treated it with astringent medicines, and that does not work; then you must restrain it with a gold wire, because silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth; and if you want to straighten the teeth, take the wire and wind it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the loose teeth between the teeth that are good, if there is one or more, until you reach a healthy tooth on the other side; then start the wrapping again up to the part where you began, and pull your hand subtly and gently so that it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.  
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the bone with pliers and assemble them, and place it between the healthy teeth so that it does not stain the tongue.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is knocked out, if one puts it back in its place, again and again, as we have said; and no one intervenes who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes one makes the shape of a cow bone tooth, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and removes it as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the ligature of the tongue 
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligature comes from under the tongue naturally, as one is born; or by accident of a sewn wound; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold his head in your lap, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligature broadly, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment, and if there is hardness or knot, and it is from the sewing of a wound, then insert the hook and cut the ligature broadly; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery which is underneath; and when you have done so, lift the area with rose water and alum, or with cold rose water, then put under the tongue a linen tent; and the patient should wash it every night so that the wound does not close. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood flows, put powdered vitriol on the spot; and if it does not stop, cauterize it with a lentil-shaped cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is of a dark color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is inclined to become white, and there is moisture, cut it with a scalpel, and make an incision with a fine spatula, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if it still bleeds in your work, put powdered vitriol on it until it is extinguished, then return to your work until you have removed all the pus; then lift the place from its surroundings, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat 
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes boils come inside the throat which are called "godath", and we properly call them the two tonsils, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the evacuation of blood; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will cut it, or it would break on its own; and if it is whitish in color and the root is thin, have the instrument ready to cut, but first look to see if the abscess is warm, at rest and appeased. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and let his hands be on your breast, and open their mouth and take the scalpel in your hands, and press the tongue down below with the instrument, so that it is shaped like this; and it should be of silver or a thin iron as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Don't press the tongue against all these instruments, and see the abscess. Take the lancet and put it into the almond, and force it upwards as much as you can; and do not draw anything from the cloths with it. Then apply the instrument to the abscess, in which form it seems a strength; but the head is bent, and one side against the other, and they are very sharp, and are made of steel or iron: 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, take the forceps, in which form it is:  
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other. And when you have grasped one of the almonds, grasp the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water that is sweet and mild. If bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with hot water, or decoctions of pomegranate rinds are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then cure it until it is healed; and if other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, cut them as you did the two almonds. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, to be precise, a small-sized abscess; and she had almost completely closed off her entire throat so that the woman could not breathe through the passage which was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she remained like this for one or two days. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had forced two reins through the two holes where it was born. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then and inserted a scalpel into one of the holes, then I drew out a large portion of pus; then I proceeded in the other hole where it was born, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards, I inserted the scalpel into these abscesses and drained a part of them, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of her throat was cleared, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess would grow again, filling the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I lanced it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it remained without growing; and I departed from these parts, and only God knows what happened to her after me. 
de l’uve	of the eye 
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When a cold descends to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below large and round, it is called "eye". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the boil below has subsided, and it is subtle, then it is fitting that you cut it; and the one which is round, gathered, and not long; and it is bloody or of a yellow color or black, then it is fitting that you make an incision. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient. 
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is fitting then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument which we have mentioned before; then insert the lancet into the eye, and draw it beneath, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.  
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is fitting that you not cut away more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut away more, it grieves the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and heal it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears being cut, it is fitting that you apply something to cauterize the sense of fear. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cautery is sharp and piercing. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient put his head in your hand, and then press his tongue against the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cautery, and hold with a sharp, lively grip so that it is not too thick nor too thin; and use the point of this instrument, from which comes the form: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And he says that on the head where one puts the medicine, like the hair of a spoon, and put the instrument all over the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the bleb; then hold your hand all over the medicine and press it on the eye for half an hour, as long as you see it shrink and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you see fit, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument all the way into the cotton on top, as long as the cotton burns on the eye; and do this often until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and leave it alone for four or five days. And if you need to start the cautery again from the medicine, start it again, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse that which is around the medicine; and keep it cool with cold water and cure it with gargles until it is healed. 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calamus and wormwood and oregano and rue and chamomile and lavender and similar herbs, and gather them all together or some of them in a pot, and put in water and let it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot let there be a tool fitted according to this manner: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or iron, and let one end be put in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through a tube until the eye is mortified; then repeat this often until the eye dries up, and make sure that you do not do this at the beginning of the arrival of the hot abscess, because many things can happen; and do not do this except when the hot abscess declines. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put inside the head a crust of egg, so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot; for the crust of egg does not make the vapor burden the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with salvation. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fishbone, or something else lodges in the throat. Therefore it is necessary that you draw out what you can see and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument so that you see the thing move; and that which does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if it extracts the thing through vomiting. Or the patients swallows a piece of sponge or a piece of navel or a root of lettuce or a piece of stale bread. And tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it. And when it comes to its place, it will come out, and then you will draw it out; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take an instrument according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the patient's head raised high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest he lose his voice, or push any bone inside; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows where the thing is airy; if it goes down, or he pulls it back evenly with the whole instrument, as long as it is pulled back. 
de la sansue de la gorge	from the back of the throat 
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes medicine is enough for the back of the throat as I have said in the division by means of remedies; and when this does not help, then look into the patient's throat towards the sun, while you press his tongue with the instrument that I have told you about. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the back of the throat, pull it out with a small hook or with fine tongs that are suitable for this.  
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a dog's hair and put it in the throat of the patient, then put the tip of the iron into the hair while it is hot and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And keep the patient thirsty every day. 
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water and open the mouth and pour it in without letting him swallow and move his hand often; and as soon as he feels the water, he will cry out.  
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if he does not cry out as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times for it will fall out without resistance. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The way to fumigate is that you take a pot with live coals in it, and cover it with a cloth pierced in the middle, and put the head of the instrument through the hole; then pour in your fumigation, and have the patient put the end of the cane in his mouth and close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape but goes straight to his throat; and now the object will fall out.  And if it does not cry out, begin the fumigation many times again; let the patient thirst, and eat salty and sour things, and do not drink water; then it is necessary for it to come out by this method. 
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the sinus, if it is such that one can see it, resembles tongs curved to enter into the throat; and it has a resemblance to the beak of a bird, and it has the roughness of a file so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and look at the shape: 
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses  
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many types of abscesses are, according to what memory comes here after one and the other in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its appearance itself, and from what it holds moisture. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is by the places where they are on the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses on the head are different from those on the buttocks, and abscesses in fleshy places are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if an abscess should not be pierced, as long as the pus is mature according to its completion; and if there are those that should be pierced when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left until it is ripe around, it may happen that the ligament and nerve of the joint become corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is near a principal limb, and you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal limb; if it is near the fundament, pierce it even if it is not ripe; and it is not right that you pierce a ripe abscess without complete digestion, except for the one that is near the fundament, so that it ripens completely, and is elongated inside, and fistula may develop; and it cannot heal in a long time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess which is death according to fulfillment, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of the fever, and the diminishing of the pain and redness, and in the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation or more depending on the place of the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the perforation be the length of the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their equal places where there is no weeping. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that weep, according to that member. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, if it moves it is worth leaving the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it in front of them, the body will be lengthened by the venom from it, and is full of a lot of filth; and perhaps the lips and the depths of it harden. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are any abscesses that are pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what its members may need. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is fitting that you administer small abscesses, small holes; and in large abscesses, large holes, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is fitting to sever the core, and cover; when it has become as hard as a cloth, and is mortified, it is fitting to do as one does for buboes: and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such that one covers as the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of the ankles; and if there are such where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as a superficial abscess, it befits you to pierce it fully; and when the abscess is large, and it has gathered much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at that hour, but draw out some of it. Then poultice the abscess until the next day, then draw out something more; do this many times in stages, until all the pus is drawn out; likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old decrepit men. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit leaps sometimes with the discharge of pus, and it may happen that the patient dies, and you do not blame yourself. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a clean incision, apply strips of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many holes, it befits you to place a strip in each one so that they come against each other; and if you have found a piece of skin within the abscess which has been cut around, fill it with old cotton or lint from linen free of moisture, and bind it until the third day. Then unbind it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold, clean water and moisten a cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding continues, apply a bandage and dressing, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is wintertime, and the wound or abscess is very sensitive, then you should put on cloths moistened with wine and hot oil; and if it is summertime, and the wound is fleshy, then you should put on cloths moistened with water and oil, or with wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess, wipe it, and dress it as appropriate, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what you should universally know in the treatment of abscesses; I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter. 
des soros	of sores 
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come on the head, they are like threads woven together, as like the seam of a tunic, and many of them resemble each other. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some are greasy and some have moisture like boils; and if there are such that are hard and stony at the waist, there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose it.  
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the waist are such that you should try all instruments called "entrometteurs," whose form comes afterward, what it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, so let it flow through for a long time. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, scrape away without leaving any skin that contained it, because it will return if you leave anything; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; this will carry away what remains at night. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin again the cotton, as before, the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain at night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable to it, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds a lot of fat, so cut it according to this form, long; and he throws on his ointments, and flay it from all sides, and put all your care of milking for the coat where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do what I told you after. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this for an abscess if it is pierced, and in the waist and in the groin as I told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the pierced abscess and the pus is lighter, because they are few drops of blood.  
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or the head where there is no moisture, and of these were the abscesses that I cut or the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess also like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if someone had made any incision on it, they would have done just as well to make a wound like from a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	For other abscesses that come or rise, especially those that come at the head of children and at the roots of ears, the opening should always be in the lowest place so that the pus comes out; and treat them as is appropriate. 
des scrophules	of scrofula  
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and below the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are many, and are joined together. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own area, just as the wart and the abscess on the head, as we have said; and there are many appearances of these scrofula. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others so malignant that they will not obey health.  
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that case, which you see of good disposition to touch, and resembles the color of the body, moves in every part, and is not raised at the nerves of the neck nor at the artery nor at the duct, and is not deep; it is fitting that you cut it off from above, and scrape it from every side, and extend the two edges of the scar to one-inch lengths, if you need, as we have said in abscesses on the head; and treat it bit by bit, and be sure that you do not cut a nerve nor a vein, and let neither the scalpel nor the knife be sharp, lest your hand slip, and do not go too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not let you work, put powdered vitriol into the wound, or some powders that staunch blood, and extract the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed and the wound softened, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work until you complete it; then look with your index finger if there are any small scrofuls remaining, and cut them out and clean them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scroful, it is not fitting that you cut that scroful at its root, but tie it with a strong doubled thread, and let it fall off by itself without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton steeped in Egyptian ointment, and then dress it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you have cut out all the scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you understand how to cut out its root, and draw it out with force, and sew it as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules which retain excess, pierce them where it appears rotten; and pierce it as the one previously mentioned, depending upon it, then apply dressings with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, then apply a cure of ointment, promoting flesh, until it is healed. 
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have strabismus, it is necessary that the fold of the throat which is called the "epiglottis" be removed; and this should not be done by anyone else, because all the veins and the pores of the patient are affected in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the tonsils. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the pores, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from choking.  
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cleave the epiglottis, we must cleave it below three or four circles, a small cut across between the two circles or according to the quantity of the cut in the mucous membrane, not in the cartilage; and those who are skilled in sectioning the epiglottis will find no flesh there, and the vessels are long. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is fitting that he extend the skin of the throat to the entire width, then split the chest as long as it comes to the windpipe; and shun the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the sinew, as we have said; and it is proven by the section through the windpipe which jumps out from the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the chest, and sew it all alone without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed. 
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely torn open, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the fault lies with the windpipe. 
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then hold the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and because the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. Then they commanded to sew the wound and clean it, as long as it was cleansed; and I will tell you what I have seen. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a maiden who took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the cartilages of the windpipe; and I was called to clean it, and I found her as dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had come out of it, and even though she had not cut a vein nor any passage except the throat, the veins were severed by the wound. 
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound and treated it until it was healed; and nothing further happened to the young woman except that her voice became hoarse, and she returned afterwards to her former state; for this reason I say that there should be no fear in cutting the epiglottis. 
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat 
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of wine, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; in the natural kind there is no cause. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	The accidental kind occurs in two ways, one of which resembles fat tissue, and the other way resembles an abscess that comes from a blood vessel; there is danger and it is not fitting to operate with fire except in those that are small, and test and search at all the openings: if you find it as soft as new fat and it does not yield to any vein, cut it out, as one cuts out warts, and treat it at its entire length, if there is any; and bind it well immediately and treat it as is fitting until it is perfectly healed. 
des nous	from us 
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways that we use, of which I will say all the resemblances; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between us and issue. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever lasting, as long as the boiling is not passed, and is completed the putrefaction; then rests the fever and the heat. 
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a boil there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins also as a small pea, and becomes large; and they are according to two resemblances, either fatty or moist, and much of color are as I have said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a boil, that you probe and inquire first with all the instrument which is called "introducer," according to what its shape will come or chapter which is after. 
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to inquire into abscesses of us is that you take the wettest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the center, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the interposing thing, and be careful that it does not jump out. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs out, whatever color it is, if it comes forth as I have said of the other abscesses; and if after the interposing thing no moisture comes, know that it is greasy, so then cut it in a cross shape, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape it on each side and keep the skin where it lies so that you draw it out healthy with the new growth; and if you cannot draw it out healthy, draw it out piece by piece so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains there nothing, the nerve returns many times; and if one part remains, and it does not grieve him, apply the wound with some corrosive powders, and extract the wound, and put soothing things on hot abscesses, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the nerve is large, cut the two edges of the wound, and cure it according to what enflames flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein pulsating is contrary to you or another hastens you and apply the place of ground vitriol, and leave it for II days or III, until the wound rots, and relieves the boiling of blood; then return to cutting what remains in the nerve. 
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of inserting instruments, and they are of three manners: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three of these: large, medium, and small, to encircle fistulas abscesses; and they are also like the needles with which we cut off warts, and they are made of citrine iron, or silver, and those tinged yellow are worth more, and are better proven with black lead to encircle the bends of fistulas; and they are of three manners: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of lancets are of much similarity, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are lancets which have two curves in three ways also; and there are lancets which have three curves, and are also in three ways; and there are lancets which have two curves, and lancets of one curve only, and are in three ways; and all this is necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these that we use are sharp, and there are some which do not cut except on one side, with which we scrape the skin, so that we do not cut the vein nor the nerve; and among these are introducers made up like handles, so that the patient does not notice them when opening abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes one uses another instrument small and resembling a butcher's scraper, according to this shape, with which we cauterize blood. 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it back in place where it heals by joining of veins, and arteries, and never return according to this great form: 
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, so much so that they look like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form from this line .b. to .g.: 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine ointment containing charcoal, then bring together the two edges of the wound by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs down, and is softened by its size as it happens in women, then cut it into two ribs above, by two similar slits; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to line .g.; then scrape off the skin that is between the two edges, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with softened cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it softens the remaining fat, then treat it until it is healed.  
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits 
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come below the armpits are types of hard scrophula where there are ribs, and some contain moisture. 
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those then that contain moisture it is fitting they be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.: 
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, apply the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and cure it with ointment suitable for this until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrophula, do it as we have said for incisions of scrophula, and if the wound runs pus, apply a cautery as we have said before. 
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery 
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it is joined, there often come many abscesses, and the same happens when a vein is swollen and has an abscess; and if the knowledgeable one knows when it is for the artery, the abscess is long and straight; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel it pulling away; and when it is for the vein, it appears round and deflated; and it is foolishness to cut this abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits and at angles or at the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
