Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to remove the iron cure, and also the one who is in charge, and in the one that is swollen from a ruptured artery make a long incision over the skin; then operate with the size of your fingers, and neatly separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed; then insert a needle under it and make it pierce through to the other side, and remove the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then point the place between the two ties with an intromissor until the pus that is there comes out, and the abscess is released; then apply a cure that contains balm, as long as the ties hold; then treat it with ointment suitable for this type of thing, as long as it heals; and if the abscess is in the size of a vein, you must hold what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then insert the needle under the place that you are holding, and make it pierce through, and put in a double thread so that you pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I told you, or tie one of the two ends with the two threads; and if you doubt that the threads will come loose, insert another needle into all the thread under the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and remove the threads in four places; then cut the abscess so that the excess comes out, then cut away the excess of the flesh and leave what is tied; then put a softened cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply cures of tents and ointments until it heals. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves 
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are injured, or by too much hard work, and similar things. 
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	This happens more often in the shoulders and arms and throughout all their joints, and this is a grievous abscess, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it is in several positions without pain; and when it is removed, the patient feels pain, and it is not the same as the flesh, but below the heart; and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and that which is in the joints should not be covered with iron: for fear of contraction; and that which is on the head or forehead, make a cut with a scalpel. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it from an incision, and scarify it, then the bone should be exposed and the wound assembled by sutures, and cured until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging 
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the bellies and not elsewhere, a disease called "funge" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and its root is subtle, and its head large; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and they were split open, and there was always moisture flowing out. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found that one weighed XVIII ounces, and the other VI 3., and the operation is such that if you look and see that the patient is moist, and the color of the cartilage is white and moist and has a subtle root; then cut it with a scalpel wide, and have the fire cautery ready.  
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the waist there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if it does not stop, then cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of iron, then take thread made well and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it two days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to tighten the thread until it stops the artery, and bleeds through its work; and if the roots are large, fear to cut yourself in the belly, but you can well cut half, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful that you do not cut the nerve which is of a dark color and poor sense and milky appearance.  
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an ulcerated abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers afterwards. 
quant li boude ist fuer	When the arm is strong 
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the arm comes from cautery of wound or cleavage of flesh, and is on the belly and in some of the bowels, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that cuts from veins or arteries according to what is in front, or from windiness; and if it is from the rupture of the flesh and by the exit of the bowel, then is the color of the abscess resembling the color of the body, and is a light thing without pain, and appears from diverse exits. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its two sides it will answer back, and then return, and by chance if it is tightened, and enlarges much at the entrance of the bath and by great exertion. 
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is from moisture, it is a light thing and appears well when you press it with your hand and it does not constrain at all; and if it is from blood, then it appears by these signs: the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is from windiness, then it is soft to the touch, and the works are such that you see if the appearance is from the blood of the artery, or vein, or windiness.  
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the care. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his belly, and be extended straight out, then sign a circle all around the abdomen; then command him to grasp often between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed with your entire spatumile, then extend half of the abscess above at all the great uncine; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the knot be loose; then work on half of the extended abscess upon the tie, and put your index finger in, and search for the intestine; if you find it caught by the tie, untie it, and put the intestine out through the opening of the belly; and if you find the bowel, grasp it with the uncine, and cut away the excess; and if the artery works against you, or the vein, go carefully around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads in them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross so that you pierce through; then pull the abscess in four places onto the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it rots, and let the dead flesh come off by itself; or cut it away when it becomes subtle and rotten, then cure the place as is necessary, and sew up the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as is necessary, and suture the place. 
dou chancre	where a sore 
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the resemblances of a sore, and how one must work by medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and we say that the sore enlarges in the flesh, and great caution is needed in its cure, and the ancients said that when a sore is in a place where it can be scraped off, such as a sore which is on the breasts, and on the thighs, and in similar places, one must remove it all when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it does not behoove you to approach it, for I have never been able to heal any, nor has anyone ever healed any before me. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient several times with black bile; then make him fast if he has manifest repletion, then put the patient in a good place to do the work; then cut your oncines or sore, and shave all around, and bone all around without leaving anything; and let the blood run out completely, and wash the place well with your hand or something else, and if the running of blood prevents you from making the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then cure it with another cure until it is healed. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what manner the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is only erupted; and one should not touch iron in these two resemblances: to wit, tympanites and hypoarche, for it is a mortal thing; so when you medicine this resemblance of dropsy which is called "erupted" with medicine, and the cure does not profit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and loosening of the bowels and similar things; then do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient is of strong constitution, and he has no other illness than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must work thus: lay the patient straight upon your hands, and let the attendants press the belly at the end by pushing the water to the lowest part below the hip, then take the spatulet with a pointed end according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cutting of two parts. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At a point, and in no way let it be so inserted that it can reach the intestines when you put it in, nor can it pierce; then look to see if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if it is fitting that you cleave into them below the navel three fingers' width to the right on the loin; and if the dropsy is for the illness of the liver, let your incision be to the left of the navel three fingers' width; and if it is for the spleen, let it be to the right, and it is not fitting that the patient lies upon the incision lest superfluities run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push it in, and lift your hand at all the scalpel between the skin and the flesh as much as when paring to the quantity of a nail or thereabouts; then pierce the flesh until the scalpel comes to the eighth place, and this is the place of the sharp point, then pull hard, and push this instrument which has this form: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a subtle silver cane, and is made of iron or light artichoke, and has in the lower part one small hole; and on one side there are three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is shaped like a feather pen, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes use to cut the quill: 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the handle, so that when the instrument comes to a point, now draw it back on the instrument; empty out then one half or one third part because if you empty out more than what is right at that time, by chance the patient might die due to his spirit separating from the body, or his flesh may rot, or he may approach death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and his pulse; then treat the instrument and hold back the point, and it is now held for the heart which stops up the hole that is on the syfac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then start the instrument again the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw out a small quantity from the point; do this every day, and beware of drawing so much out that there remains but a drop of blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient and leave a lot of water in him, then use the cure of burial or hot sand, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun; and let him drink; and the cure of drying medicines until he is healed; and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the foreskinning of the penis 
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who do not have an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary soon as he has not pierced through all the spatula very subtly according to this form:  
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then put a small opening with a sharp tip, and tie it and leave it so for III days or IV and when he wants to urinate, remove the tie and let him urinate, then replace it; and by chance none may be needed because the urine that comes out will not allow it to close. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose anus is small, if it is treated with a plum stone as we have said, then it will enlarge. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have their anus in its place are unfortunate, for none are born who have the anus at the head of the penis, because they cannot urinate before lifting their penis upward; and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot come up to the vulva, and this is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of the operation is this: the patient lies on his back; then they extend the head of the penis and cut it as large as a feather so that the anus falls in the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding which often occurs, and if it happens, have the one who stops blood stop it, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis 
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these sores come on the penis, and they are an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; it is fitting that you take them with a sharp lancet, and cut and cleanse all of them, then put softened cotton with Egyptian ointment on top; then cure him with diafinition ointment until he is healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the sore is malignant, of a foul color and discharging, it is fitting that you apply a cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the sore is at the top of the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is fitting that you remove the part that is inside first; and when it is sewn up, then you care for the outside part. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all together, unless the flesh of the penis is well secured so that it is not pierced, blackness and corruption come to his penis and testicles; it is fitting to cut away everything that is black and corrupted, then bind an adhesive plaster made of honey and flour which is made from pomegranate rinds and vinegar on top, then treat him with other remedies until he is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding comes, apply the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries help in two ways together: that is to say, in the stopping of bleeding, and in corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is fitting that you draw or pull a cane of lead from the penis and make the patient urinate through it; and when the hairs burn at the head of the penis which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or there is a sore or abscess, then it is fitting that you scald it with a heated instrument until the bonds are loosened and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if this is a difficult thing to do, it is fitting that you scald it with a spatula in a few places at the head of the penis and on the skin; then separate them well between the two and put a fine linen cloth softened in cold water so that it does not burn immediately. 
de la circoncision	Of circumcision 
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a simple matter of continuation like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our own volition, and especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for salvation. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience. 
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I want the greater part of the masters and saints who performed circumcisions did so around the tenth day, and with force, and with a single instrument; if it were cut deeply for there are two layers, and by chance one is severed above and the other remains below. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Then it must be cut again, and the pain is doubled, and at ten days the point of the member is not securely cleaned; and when cleaning the foreskin, the iron may slip, ruining the work, and many times they are born so that they need no cleaning and I have wanted this. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the modification which is made to all the thread of the line I have found the goodness of the experiment for the forces cut precisely both above as below. 
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, if you cut equally in I all the time; but let the thread be well twisted around the leather; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are not doing anything to him except tying the thread around the penis just only, and then let him rejoice in all the ways that you can; then let him stand between your hands straight, and put the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the penis and blow on it, or suck on it, and pull it up as high as the head of the penis is in; then cleanse it well from the filth which has gathered there, then tie the marked place with a double thread, then tie it under the other tie; and hold it with two fingers by the second ligature to the pouch and the index finger, and cut between the two ties, then quickly remove the heart above it and pull the head of the penis; then let the blood run little by little, for that is the best; and put powder on it, and on the powder put a plaster glued with half an egg yolk cooked tempered with rose water, confected with good fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed. 
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forceps for purification is this: the two jaws should be held tight and sharp, and the jaws should be as large as the handle equally. 
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of purification occurs when the core comes out at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your fingernail, just as the pus face an abscess; and the cap equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, take it with pliers and then cut it. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and that which is below the glans penis is swollen, leave it until the abscess boils are appeased, and lightly scrape it; then cut as you can move, and beware of the part of the glans penis, for it will not harm anything. 
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat then the place of things within a wound with powder, which we have said or treated in powders, and if you cut too much core, and it goes up, it will not harm anything; treat it then, as we have said, until it is healed. 
dou retenement de l’urine	For the retention of urine 
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine may be due to a stone, or congealed blood, or the bowel, or a tumor, or similar things, which we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone which is at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent on his knees; and let his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly above his back, and restrain the patient from moving as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder will be forced towards the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer an extraction with any instrument called a "syringe", of which this is the form: let it be made of fine silver light in weight, like the quill of a bird; and let the cane be a palm and a half long, and let it be fine at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of drawing out the urine is such that you take a doubled thread and tie it to the head of a bit of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut off the excess of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and yolk of egg, and make the patient sit on a seat, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and lukewarm water; then gently put the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis above towards the buttocks; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and let the patient feel it coming up to the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless because the one who guides it where it goes is crooked; then pull out the thread at all the wool bit by bit, and the urine follows the wool, then draw it out and let the urine flow; and begin again the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved. 
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder 
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood comes into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see sharp waters and medicines distilled, then make with all the instrument which is called a "clepsedre," and it is of this form: 
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has three holes: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the canals are made so that the medicine will pass easily through the urethra without addition, so that if one can draw out the moisture, and push it in when needed; and when you see the medicines flow into the bladder, put the end of the catheter into the moisture, and pull on the string which is inside; pull the moisture towards the catheter, and then tighten the string well inside; the moisture will enter inside, and will come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder: it is as follows: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is made of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and below at the breast where the arm bone joins; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in which you see to cleanse the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts formed with a good strong thread, and heat the pot with that moisture over the fire; then put the head of the enema into the penis, and hold your hand on the bladder with all the moisture coming up, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it round about; then put a strong thread through those holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a bowl, and put in what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it into the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stone and the extraction together with medicines; and we have said the difference between a retained stone in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should work by incision; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly. 
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is retained in the bladder happens more often in children, and the sign of it is that sharp pain jumps from the bladder resembling sharp pain in its subtlety; and it opens widely, and grates the patient's penis, and he can urinate many times, and then becomes rigid; and with many of these pains, urination stops; and healing is easy for children until they are four years old, and it is very grievous in old people, and moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.  
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is fitting first to purify the patient by enema, to draw out all the phlegm which is in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and push and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from there; then make him sit between your hands evenly balanced, and let his hands be below his thighs so that the bladder is completely sloping downwards; then search for and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut upon the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if you do not feel it at all upon touching, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is an infant, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young man fully grown; and insert it into their fundament and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, hold it at the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger, and push it outwards where you see to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend the testicles upward with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the testicles in the part where the circumcision is made; then he inserts the spatulum cutting tool, which has this form: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And it enters between what is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left buttock; and let it be straight on the stone, and its two points be then at the fundament, and let the incision be made so that it is wide outside, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; by chance press with the point which is at the fundament, so that it jumps out without work; and know that there are some stones which have angles, and edges: these are harder to extract; and there are some which are below, resembling a bean, and round, from which the exit is easy. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	Where there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must pull it out with tongs which are also like a file at the head, to remove the stone so that it does not escape; or you insert a subtle instrument bent at the head; and if you cannot get it in this way, enlarge the hole, and if the flesh is cut, remove it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, insert the largest first into the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull it out hard, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are several. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be sewn up, and make a larger wound. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out immediately because the veins cannot be joined; but nevertheless strive to draw it out, or to break it with tongs, as long as you draw it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, bathe the wound with frankincense and aloes and dragon's blood, and remove it, and put a soft cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water on top, to soothe the hot abscess; then raise the patient on his pillow, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, if it rises well with oil and water, then treat it with diachylon ointment and basil ointment until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses should come in the wound and corrosions, and congealment of blood in the bladder, and it be retained by this, urine which is known in part manner that without leap with the urine: put then your fist in the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and rot it; then lift the wound with water and alum and salt, and help it in all ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is fitting that every hour that you treat it, that you tie the two thighs together, and apply the medicines upon the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in a conduit of the penis, and stuck within, and the urine cannot issue; so treat it as I have said above, that you cut it many times, and one excuses the cutting by this treatment. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already seen this happen like this. 
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron forceps according to this shape and let it be fixed at three angles in the fire.  
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then insert the forceps into the shaft gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the forceps in your hand on the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone through; urine will soon come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the shaft. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is soon broken and comes out with the urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread below the stone and the other above, then cut the shaft in the place of the stone between the two ligatures, then extract it forcefully, and untie the ligature, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.  
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women 
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It can happen that a stone is lodged in women, and if it ever happens, the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to expose herself to the mirrors, especially when she is chaste.  
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a woman who knows well this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper lodged than the stone of man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessities demand it, it behoves you to take a midwife who knows well, and at pains one finds her, and if you don't find her, not even one chaste, but subtle mirror; and present her with a wise woman experienced in the life of women, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and command her that she do what you command her from the inquiry of the stone; and look very well whether the woman is a virgin: then it behoves you to thrust your finger or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrict it under her finger, and recommend that she thrusts her finger or with it into the patient, and want and press her left hand on the bladder above.  
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is fitting that she moves it from the entry of the bladder down below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then put it on the stone at the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the bone, where it is movable and palpable, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her foot above the stone or below, and let the incision be small at first; then push the knife into the incision, if you feel the stone so enlarge the wound as much as the stone may come out strong, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those which have horns. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the resemblances to know the outcome. 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the vein bursts, put powdered vitriol on the spot and hold it for an hour until the vein is cauterized; then return to your work as long as the stone is strong, and have the instruments that I told you in the extraction of a stone from men to help you in your work; and if the vein bursts, and it is an artery that is cut, put the powder on the spot and bind it with tents and bandages, and do not begin again this one, and leave the stone and do not draw it out, lest the patient die by chance; then heal the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the swelling subsides, you may return to your work, as long as the stone is strong. 
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia 
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A watery branch is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white yolk, which is below the heart of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called "yolk," and sometimes it is properly in the web of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white yolk that we have said; and this does not break off.  
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and it is spread out matter. 
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: either it is a declining color to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is the white yolk that we have said, it is a boiled down abscess, the rupture long as the shape of an egg, and does not open the testicles, for it has moisture all around.  
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the very fabric, then the abscess will be sewn with one part of an egg, and for this reason one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white sinew, then he feels it well; therefore when you see to know the color of the moisture, try it throughout the instrument, whose shape is described above. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, which comes after the instrument, judge what is inside. 
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is fitting that the patient be healthy according to our ability and the repletion of his body; then lay him on his back, on something a foot high, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on his right, and extend the foreskin to one of the two ribs near the heart of the testicles; then take the scalpel, sharp and clean, and cut the skin of the testicles between them lengthwise down to the base; and let your incision be straight, dividing the skin of the testicles up to the white sinew, and delicately scrape it according to our ability; then pierce the sinew full of pus with a large opening, and extract all the pus, and then put on your ointments, and spread the sinew upward; and do not touch the heart of the testicles, but only the sinew itself; cut all or piece by piece very carefully the side of it, so that if you do not cut it wisely, the pus will return; and if the egg leaps out during your work, put it back in its place when you have finished the work on the sinew; then bring together the two edges of the heart of the testicles with a suture, then treat it as other wounds, until it is healed.  
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspensory, in doubt of the flow of blood; then cut the scrotum at all the suspensory, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the artery is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put into the wound linen moistened with rose oil; and put another linen moistened with wine and oil on the two scrotums, and put doubled cloths on top, and tie it all up according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and make them of shredded linen according to this appearance and let them be joined by stitching at the throat of the breeches, and one of the ends takes hold on the fundament up to the back, and the other at the side where the knife is; and the other two chiefs on the two angles, and let all the binding be assembled in the loop of the breeches; and never is this branch medicined with a cautery instead of an iron blade, and it is that you take a subtle culinary cautery, and cut the skin of the scrotums, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white membrane which contains the artery is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that membrane with small holes, and scorch it with this subtle hot cautery:  
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cup in all ways that you can, so long as you scrape everything; and guard that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and be careful to prevent bleeding, and more careful than surgical works; and if anything opposes you, whether an abscess or bleeding or something else, treat what opposes you, according to what is said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, then perform a perforation as I tell you, and know that when you are well certain by the signs we have said that the watery humor is there, then have the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess below at the whole breadth of the thumb, and make the perforation as long as the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the pus may flow out; then put cotton on the place and bind it, and leave it to drain the remaining pus, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the pus to flow out at the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a quill or the instrument with which we treat the pus of dropsy, of which form is described before; and widen the opening of the wound, and know that the pus returns and gathers again after six months or thereabouts, and when it has gathered as before, then the patient will pass his days. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the thighs 
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there are many dangers due to which it seems to me better to leave it; and I will tell you the work and the appearances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come on bodies, and especially on the thighs; and this is in many cases. 
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know by an excess of sharp and hot humors which are spread on the thighs or from percussion; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and it does not find any pain, and is a grievous abscess; and perhaps there are painful and hard abscesses, dark in color, and sometimes it comes from a new artery or swelling of a vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a new artery, it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess when you press it with your fingers; and it is not fitting that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of a vein swelling is known by its arrangement to the expression from the touch of the two fingers and one can well make the cut on this resemblance and on the other carts; and it is that you cut the heart of the onions then raise the egg on high, and draw the thread through the white part, and deliver the suspensory from all sides of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already soldered with these carts new, then it is fitting that you draw the egg and cut it; and if it is airy at the white part, or in that which is inside the vessels, then it is fitting that you deliver all that tension, and cut roundly. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the origin of the cart is or is behind, then it is fitting that you cut it all and extract the egg as we have said. 
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is complete, apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of an abscess of the testicles 
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a boil, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient groans when he walks; and the treatment for this illness is as perilous as the one before it, nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then loosen the scrotum of the testicles down to your knees, separating all the vessels which are close to the penis, and hold the masters, and stretch them out; then cut with a wide sharp scalpel at the transverse point where the vessels are exposed, then flay from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples; then insert a needle with double thread and tie it to the first place where the vein has come, and tie it directly to the other end; then cut them straight in the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted humors; then treat the wound like the others where you inject broth, so that no vessel ruptures that nourishes one of the testicles; for by this there is no harm, but if all the vessels become visible, it is necessary to drain the testicles from all the vessels; so that the testicle does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry out and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of a break of the bone 
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch are due to the section that comes from the bone or the extension on the belly in the part of the groin for which the intestines descend from this break to one of the bowels; and this break is either of the bone or of the extension of it, and these two ways come from many causes: either by percussion, or by jumping, or by brawling, or by lifting a heavy weight, and similar things. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the bone, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and the abscesses appear diverse under the skin nearby, and this is due to the exit of the intestines and the body outside of the bone. 
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never separate the intestines with the nerves, and they are held together, and cause the patient great pain to suffer, even when pressed. 
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron out of fear, for which it is advisable to avoid them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;
