et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the operation is such that you command the patient to pull the intestine with his hand inside the wound, if he can get it in; then hold it squeezed between your hands and lift the thighs; then stretch the heart above, and cut all the skin of the testicles along the length; then put the levers of the hip bone into a cinch according to what you need to open the wound, and let them be such that the bowels can come out; then flay the loose tissue that is under the skin of the testicles until the white fibrous tissue is exposed on all sides; then put your index finger into what follows the testicle, between the white fibrous tissue which is under the skin of the egg, and between the second fibrous tissue; and separate what is behind the egg, and between the second fibrous tissue; and then push with your right hand into the heart of the testicles, and stretch the white fibrous tissue upwards with your left hand and lift the testicle towards the hip with all its fibrous tissue; and command the assistant to extend the testicle upwards, and loosen what is behind the ligature; and feel with your fingers if there is any intestine entangled or white fibrous tissue, and if you find anything, put it back into the belly below; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and push it into the rear part of the fibrous tissue which is after the skin of the testicles; after the hip bone, then cut the ends that appear from the threads, until there are four threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the fibrous tissue which we have said is under the skin of the testicles with a strong ligature of two parts; then wrap the ends of the threads and tie them in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish it can enter, and no abscess can come; and place the ligature according to the first ligature long two finger widths from it, and after these two ligatures leave the fibrous tissue which is under the heart of the testicles a thumb's width; and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the testicles until the sinews are severed; and the bowel, as we have said before; then apply wool soaked in oil and place it on the wounds, and apply the ligature that we have mentioned. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white flesh as we have said after incision out of fear of blood clotting. 
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and leave the ligature as long as it bleeds by itself; and if it delays in ceasing, it should be moistened with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it bleeds; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia 
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to make the cure with iron. 
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made as in the branch which is together with it, in part the way you tie the vessels, after cutting above slightly below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess of he who works, until the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.  
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the angres, as we have said, and opens the veins; and no intestines should be drawn out of the joints, and if any are drawn out, it is bad, and they should be repaired every hour; and nonetheless, if it remains too long in this condition, the wound or sinus grows, as long as the intestine is drawn out; and this happens through the extension of the sinus which is in the angres, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and swollen, and opened; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies often on their back between your hands, then you cut the place of the fracture swollen broadly according to the quantity of three fingers; then you extract the sinus which is below the skin where it swells up, then take a red-hot iron and put it on the apparent place of the sinus; and press it firmly against the belly, then sew the two apparent veins of the sinus onto the head of the iron, and sew one and the other; then you remove the head of the iron, and do not cut the sinus nor stretch the vein or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the ramification of the intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, let the patient wash and dress the wound until it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The cautery is constrained and has no appearance in the rupture; and the cauteries are milder in this place and closer to safety. 
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles 
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the cords within are softened, and it is made to be seen; and it is necessary, when one wishes to cure it, that one make the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin upon the natural skin; then join the two lips with a suture, and if you see fit, sew first the superfluity of the softened skin at three or four sutures firmly; then cut between the sutures, and cure as other wounds, until it is healed, and draw out the thread.  
dou chastrement	Where cautery 
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that cautery is forbidden in our law, and for this reason it would please me not to speak of it in this book; but it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the master should be able to answer when asked about it, and know the cure; and the other, because we often need to cauterize certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, cats, and other animals. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cautery is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.  
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water until its testicles are softened and hanging; then we take them with our hand until they are retracted and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the castration of animals: it is necessary that you hold the animal, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut on each testicle at one cut, when you have well skinned them; and leave no puncture so that the strong sinews and the fine sinews which are on the vessels remain; and this manner of castration is better than that which is done by attraction, because by attraction there may remain by chance some part of the testicles, by which the animal desires lust; then heal the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites 
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners like men: one is that between the two testicles there appears also as the form of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes it urinates in the direction. 
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has upon the shoulder like a rod and two horns. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for the man and the woman is that you cut off all the added pieces, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, men whose urine leaks through the skin of the horns, have no cure. 
de la tentigene	of the tenting gene  
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tentigene is an added piece on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure.  
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is fitting that you hold the superfluity of the tentigene in your hand or on your knee, and cut it lightly; and do not go too far so that blood does not flow, then treat it with other treatment until it is healed; and to another piece that is born at the mouth of the womb, and the navel, and perhaps jumps out, and is according to the appearance of a cow, and therefore they called it the ancient "cow disease". 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cut it as we have said above, and treat it until it heals. 
de erratique	of wandering 
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is erratic when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the pertus is small; and it is by nature at birth, or by accident from illness that has come to be; or it is by excess of flesh, or by subtle vapor or species, and it is made complete in the womb, or on the sides, or below, or wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps having flowers; and the knowledge of this is by looking at the belly. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swellings are close and apparent, on either side or to the right.  
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is by subtle vapor, and it is close to the two leaves, do this quickly: put your two index fingers together, and have the woman on her back, spread her legs; then stretch the two leaves as much as possible, so that the subtle vapor is gone, and the swellings are removed; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and put it on the spot, and make the woman lie with a man every day, so that he cannot sleep.  
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the bone is hard and thick, it is fitting that you cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is from a sharp weapon, suspend it to the oncine and cut it; have medicines that staunch blood, such as alum, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg yolk; then apply a bandage of flax wide enough so the wound cannot close; and so it shall be for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then it shall be cured by other cures until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a sharp weapon comes in the flesh, it is fitting to cut according to this manner, except if it is a boil or ulcerated abscess. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an ulcerated abscess that is in the flesh, one should not touch it with fire. 
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids 
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which without a court usually are accustomed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become swollen; and we have said in the division the resemblances to others and signs, and I will say here those who receive a cure. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and swelling when they are ripe in the anus, and they do not appear to touch, unless cured by iron. 
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the mouth of the anus, which one can feel, are those which one can cure. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore it befits that you put the woman in a cold house, then extend the swelling with forceps, and cut off its roots, then sprinkle medicines restraining blood upon it, such as alum and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if bleeding comes, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour and mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster upon her back.  
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it goes out, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have cupping glasses applied to the back and breasts without pricking; then take flax, moisten it with plantain juice or elder juice mixed with old wine, and apply it to the area. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is at rest, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and the one called “albathir” is red, and resembles a rough head, so it must be covered as I have said for the thelul; then treat it until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marrow 
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come in the marrow, such as ulcers and putrid abscesses and herpes and swellings and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases which I have mentioned in the division.  
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I say in this treatise the hot abscess which comes in the marsh, which is not the abscesses that boil; and if you wish to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is angry at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hurry to pierce it, but let it mature until the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on a stool, and put two small stools where he can lean, and support himself on his back and bring his feet together close to the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and place his arms below his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then give him to turn towards the right side, and prepare the instrument with which one works the mouth of the abscess, of which the form will come later; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument prepared, you insert the point first in order to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is necessary that he put the tip of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument.  
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and it is gently pressed by hand, if it seems necessary to cover the head, apply a poultice of spatumile leaves; and when the bowels are emptied, put softened tents in rose oil or green oil into the wound; place the tent firmly from the edge of the wound to the margin of the abscess, and then on the margin and on the nearby skin apply clean linen moistened in water in which ivy or mallow have been boiled. Then after two days treat it with appropriate ointment until it is healed; and never lift the abscess and the wound by a clyster of water and honey, and then of water or long-boiled lily roots and aristoloche; then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound grows into the abscess, you must be careful not to cauterize it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth 
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if she sees the woman pressing down, and desiring to smell the air: then hasten the child with force so that it comes out; then you will know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue is under her head, and the placenta with it; and when you see these signs, it is appropriate to press lightly on her abdomen, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends upon its head, the placenta follows with it, and the woman is cleansed of her superfluities by good cleansing; and what comes otherwise does not come naturally.  
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes upon its feet, and the body or the shoulders and the hands come out with force, or it comes upon its stomach, or often it is converted by chance out of its neck, and by other bad figures; it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help her. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes onto her head through natural birth, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and the strength of her is weak, then make her sit on a saddle, where women hold her; and boil oil or fenugreek, and then pour the bowl between her thighs with the small spatula whose shape is this: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the second membrane, and press on her fingernail until the moisture which is inside runs out; and press on the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you should give the woman an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil; then make her drink and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child is delivered.  
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out further, then you should reset them gently bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a stool, and raise her feet up high; then overturn the stool to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall when overturned; and if the hands still cannot enter and the child is dead, then cut the hands with the knife which is previously mentioned, and extract the child, and reset it equally. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child upon its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon its feet, if it is crooked, you must straighten it upwards; and then turn it a little at a time until it is even; then take it by the feet and extend it a little at a time. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to its thighs, if he is ordered to grasp, and makes him sneeze on purpose; if the jump is strong, God willing. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as strong as we have said, then turn it a little at a time until it is according to the natural form.  
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is light. 
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come strong as we have said, take a mixture of hollyhock, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and smear with this ointment, then make her sit in tepid water up to below the ribs; and when she is softened below, give her a collar of myrrh, and put it below, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and pull out her mouth and nose, and take her belly lightly, for the child jumps now. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child onto its knees 
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if it puts its hands on its body little by little; then let it be swaddled onto its neck, and let its feet hang down, and let it lie on its back on the bed; and fold its hands little by little, and then take its hands onto its belly, and remove the cushions from underneath, as long as it is revealed downwards; and if the child does not jump, take its feet and move them upwards, then move its belly upwards, then push in its hands; and pull the child little by little; and instruct the woman to hold herself as long as the child rises. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the child who comes forth with one hand hanging down  
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	it is necessary to proceed to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, let the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, let her lie on the bed and straighten her legs; then apply the muscilage that I have mentioned; and if she does not deliver, let her sit on a chair, and then try to bring back the hand; and pull the child according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and instruct her to hold herself as long as the child rises. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child upon his neck and have spread his hands and his face turned toward the back of his mother 
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is fitting that the midwife holds her hand and then turns it little by little, and lifts it lightly; and when it is equal, she puts on the natural muscle mixture of elder and oil as we have said, then commands her to move it a little at a time; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command her to hold herself upright, and make her sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes strong in this manner for all the afterbirth, grasp the afterbirth at your finger, as long as the moisture is emptied; and if the infant leans upon his face and upon his neck, grasp it from the elbow so that it is not retained and the infant dies; then push the infant inside as long as you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to hold herself still: then draw it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the exit of twins 
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born at once; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens. 
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	What is strange and does not live is rarely named; I know that they are multiplied and separated by the placenta which divides them, which is joined to the belly; and sometimes they also issue naturally as one under another, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue crookedly, the cure is as we have said, and let the midwife be skillful, and do quickly and lightly what she does; and do as it is worthwhile for salvation.  
de plusors enfans	of several children 
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or several up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the glorious sage, and it is fitting that the midwife knows all this, for by chance similar things happen; so do according to what is fitting.  
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child 
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman who has lost her child in the womb, as I said in the division, and no fluid comes out, and you are forced to work with your hands; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound constitution and has no accident or fear of death. It is necessary for the woman to be placed on her back with her hips inclined downwards and her legs raised. And let the attendant hold her by the waist, whether she is tied to the bed so that she does not be treated in a downward direction during the removal of the child. Then rub the mouth of the woman with moist oil mixed with marshmallow and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint her hands with these oils and these mixtures. Then gently insert them into the woman's womb. Be careful where you insert the ointments so that they are suitable for this purpose; take care that if the child appears, it will descend on its head. Insert the ointments into her eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the armpit or near the ribs. If the descent is on the feet, then put them on the breastbone and lower ribs. And it is necessary to hold the ointment with your right hand and place the curve between the fingers of your left hand, and insert it gently with all your hand. Insert the ointment into any of these places that we have mentioned, until you reach the void thing. And this is the shape of the ointment:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then place it against the other pincers, or a third if you need them, so that the extraction is equal; and then stretch them equally by moving them back and forth to make it come out, and let the pincers have teeth to hold it, as its form is like this: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, smear the wound with some of its two oils, and put them in that part, and pull out the other part; and if none remains, place these pincers or higher up, and do this until it all comes out. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other and he cannot bring it back due to tightness, it is necessary that you wrap it up on a cloth until it all comes out; then cut at the jointure of the palm or with a knife, and thus you must do the same for the other hand, and for both feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is narrow in the outlet, or if it has a sharp point, then you must put the pointed spatula between your fingers and break the point and extract it; or cut it with an instrument called "almidach," from which the shape comes with the instruments or chapters that follow this one; and thus do the same if the child has a large head naturally; and then draw the bones together with forceps, and if the head jumps out and is removed by force, it must be split until the moisture which is in the lower part comes out; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture flows. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the attraction is light, and the straightening at the mouth of the womb is easy. 
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is three in the belly or breast, it is fitting that you draw it out with a drape wrapped around the hand; and make the belly or breast, as long as the moisture which is there runs; and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, then put your hand well greased from the marris, and draw it up to the mouth of the marris; then you put one or two ounces and pull hard; and if the mouth of the marris is contracted by a hot abscess which has come, it is not fitting to work on it, but it is fitting to administer moist and fatty things; and apply poultices, and those in acute softening and moistening. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it equal, then apply what we have said in the living child; and if one does not have power, then pull it hard by pieces, and do not leave anything of the afterbirth. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if he administers what we have said in abscesses that come in the marsh; and if bleeding occurs, it should be applied with a tight bandage, and he administers other remedies. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb one child had been dead, then another was conceived on top of it, and the other died too. 
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time an abscess came to her in the buttock, and it swelled so much that it opened, and began with great discharge. 
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal her, and I thought for a long time, and could not close the wound. 
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and out came a bone, and after a few days another. 
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, for the belly has no bones. 
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought these were bones of a dead child. 
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found bones within it, as long as the woman was in a better condition; and I left the woman for a long time like this, and there remained then only a little bit of swelling from the place; and I have not recounted this chapter except because, when masters find something foreign, they should know how to help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the marrow to its place 
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here afterwards comes the form of the presser, with which one presses books; and at two turns are two heads of two lines. 
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more delicate than those of the restrictor, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and its mouth should be of wood two finger-widths wide, and the edge of the branches one finger-width, and a palm and a half long; and between the two limbs there should be two adjustments of this same wood which are fastened on the one side and the other, a half-palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the marrow to open it when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, of more delicate and lighter appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood wood, according to the likeness of tongs; and it should have two jaws with two adjustments, as you see, a palm in length, and two fingers wide; and when you see the woman wanting to open her vulva for the instrument, make her sit on a bed, with her feet dangling and her legs open. Then insert the two adjustments joined together into the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all assembled, and there are many of its kinds; and when the master has prepared them, the quicker the work, and the higher the esteem for their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair of the instrument that you do not have prepared, for its necessity is inexcusable. 
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the placenta is retained at childbirth, it is fitting that you instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze on purpose, and remove your hands from her mouth and nose; and if it comes out this way, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole or cover, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in a pot in water over the fire; then put one end of a cane or tube into the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the womb, and hold it there until the vapors enter the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said.  
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint leaps quickly. 
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not strong, order the patient to wet her left hand in sesame oil or marshmallow poultice, and then put it into the opening, and seek the second joint; and when she has found it, grasp it and extend it little by little straight so that the marrow does not tear out at extraction; but you must move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come and loosen. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the marrow is constricted, we have said the treatment is sneezing and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, be careful not to pull back; but it is necessary for whoever is at the opening of the marrow, that you tie him to the thigh of the woman, then give him an enema of tetrafarmacon ointment; if he will bear it and return it, and he will come strong; but nevertheless, when he returns, there comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and harms the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is fitting, then, for fumigations to be suitable for this: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of watercress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for retention of flowers and the secondine is this: 
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it resembles a cane, and one puts the subtle point in the vagina, and the broad ends are put over the fire; and let the fumigations be upon the coals, until it is consumed, and then begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the bottom  
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have their bottom pierced, but rather it is blocked by a delicate membrane: so it is fitting for the midwife to pierce that membrane with her needle and not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and she should guard the opening so that it is not touched; then she puts linen moistened in wine and oil on it and then cures it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will remain in place, then put or insert a cane of lead, and leave it for three days, and let it be removed when the infant wants to go into the chamber. 
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this dislocation comes from the healing of a wound or an abscess; so you must cover that healing. If it is cured, as we have said of the cane of lead. 
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the fundament  
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come below the fundament are swellings and growths that come from below the fundament, or in the space between the two parts; if there is one fistula or more. And when this swelling is old, it works, and still produces moisture which brings forth white pus or subtle blood, and sometimes these fistulas persist; they are recognized by those who see them by bowel movements or flatulence when the patient defecates, and sometimes a drop of pus comes out. 
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that extend to the bladder and to the middle of the penis; and they reach the junction of the thigh and to the knee. 
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes a fistula that perforates the base and one that does not; and it is that you insert your index finger or thumb into the base, and insert a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, insert a tent of fine linen or a horsehair until you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and nothing comes out in the form of discharge, flatulence, or worms, as we have said: know that it does not perforate; if you hasten to cure it. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula penetrates to the bladder or to the urethra, the urine will spurt out and cannot be healed by medicine. 
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces as far as the joint of the thigh, then the tent comes to the place; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain around, then let it go and do not apply medicine or ointment; and in these fistulas there is nothing firmer than labor, and vanity of foolish imaginations that interfere. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is not penetrating and not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he raises his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his belly; then put in a tent of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes.  
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you must insert your index finger, and if you feel that the tent has pierced it; and whether uncovered or where you feel with your finger the synovial membrane or flesh, then you know that it is penetrating; if it does not work at all, then it cannot be healed. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	We say nonetheless that one can heal some well, but this rarely happens; and the help we do is to heat a subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula as it is said before; and put all hot in the fistula until it reaches the bottom; and do this two or three times, until you know those bad humors are burned, which are like a bird's feather; and then cure with softened tents in butter until those humors are gone, then cure with ointment anointing flesh and welding. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent enters but does not pierce as far as the bottom which is at the foundation, and there is a thick covering of flesh or pus between your two fingers and the tent, and you see the fistula behind this covering near the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula and put it forward before the tent, and then cauterize, until it reaches the head of the tent; and the tent will be freed and will fall away; then destroy those bad humors that look like a bird's feather, and leave none. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood flows freely between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or medicine. 
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cauteries bring together two good things: namely, the burning of the flesh that is added, and the stoppage of blood and drying of moisture; then treat the softened wounds with butter or chopped cheese, as long as the burns are in the wound; then treat the wound with ointments containing hard roasted charcoal, and these are dry medicines. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return. 
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way to the base of the foundation and is distant from the body, it should be pushed up to the anus or foundation, and inquire about this.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent and between them is cloth or silk or flesh, or it is close to piercing, there should be no other way but that of trust and hope through the administration of one of three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it down to the bottom, or if you can put tents in and treat it as first; do not go too far toward the bottom, lest you cut the ligament that holds the foundation, and let the excretions come forth against your will; then treat it as we have said. By chance it may be healed, or remove this covering and cleanse it after it is cut away from the foundation, either by tent or other pointed instrument. Then cleanse this spoiled flesh that is in the wound as much as you can. Then consider restoring the wound and keeping the fistula in the part beyond the foundation; which would be a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And there are never fistulas according to this manner; and when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is near or touching the foundation below the skin above, then take a pierced tent at its head according to this form: 
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put the twisted thread in II, and put the tent on all the thread in the fistula as far as its head. 
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is persistent in the margin of the foundation inside, then remove the thread from that hole, so that you put your finger or the foundation; and grasp the head of the thread, and bring the two sides together, and pull them apart from each other, and leave it for one or two days; and restrain it no more times, until the threads catch those cars which are between them, and squeak; then heal the wound until it is closed and healed. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too much constricted. 
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to make a bandage for the setting so tight, and then the cure, as we have said, until it is healed. 
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spathula which makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and dull on the other, for that reason we do not make a cut as we should not make it, as you see here. 
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners: either they are inside the fundament, just like a grain of resin, and there are some small and some large, and they often bleed, and there is one or several, and they protrude from the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that protrude have little moisture, and still bleed a little clear fluid or a little blood, and they have the color of flesh.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is fitting that you administer the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread and put it into a needle, then draw the thread over and make the needle pierce through the other side, and turn both ends of the thread under the needle; and if it is too wide, pull the thread tight, then tie a knot on the thread, and remove the needle, and do this for all the others. Leave one for correcting excess blood, then put a softened cloth moistened in rose oil or cerate on top, and command the patient to rest; and then leave it until they have healed, and when they are healed, cure them with ointment and other cures, until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	on the drying of linen or a foundation 
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is drying of flax in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use. 
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you remove the bark with the point of a spatula or your nail so that it does not become damp; then dress it until it is healed as it should be; and if it cannot heal, start the shaving again more strongly than before, until it heals a lot and is stripped; then dress it until it is healed. 
dou fremit	Where it trembles 
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formication is a small, false appearance against the body, and it goes very much in perfection; and one never finds cold, and one feels it also like the trembling of death, and it comes to all the body, and more to the hands than anywhere else. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure for it is that you take a cane from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and put that cane on the formication, so that it circles the formication all around; then turn your hand to all the cane until you grasp all around the formication, and put it in perfection, and uproot the formication from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, make one of iron or steel according to this form, and let it be thin underneath and wide on top. 
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, but hold it tight and press hard. And if you see it, cauterize the tremor as it is in front or according to the chapter on cautery. 
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of a clyster 
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or artichoke, or iron melted or hammered; and sometimes one makes these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered. 
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then that are administered in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.  
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small and large clyster is wide on top, where the belly is tied according to this manner: 
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a separation where the abdomen is tied, as you see, and the flesh is pierced within; and it has on one side II holes, and on the other I; and let the abdomen be where one puts medicines from a bladder of an animal or parchment, and be pierced all around with small holes, and have between each hole I space apart, then put into these holes I strong thread of raw silk twisted in X or some similar fashion, and assemble the abdomen as it is a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if you tie it to the instrument in front of a strong thread, then give an enema; and this is the shape of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or yolk of an egg, or something similar, then put it in gently; then squeeze the ministers with his two hands together until he is all emptied, then remove the enema, and have the patient lift his legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him strain as much as he can; and if he sleeps a whole night afterwards, it is of greater help. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize it for a stomach ailment of loosening, and the medicine hastens to go in, then repeat it until it is healed. 
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or an abscess, then the enema should be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle enema on which the skin is extracted: 
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and of medicine, according to its fulfillment. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places or parts where the wounds are made, and of what they are made. 
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the impact of a stone, and the thrust of a sword or knife, or of a lance or gun or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the places in the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the breast, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, for remembrance will come in its chapter. 
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you are careful whether it is from a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt a hot abscess: if you make it heal quickly from the cephalic vein itself if a little blood comes from the wound, and let it heal on the contrary side of the injured part; and forbid the patient to eat wine and fatty foods. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not want to heal, let his food be reduced, and do not drink wine, nor eat any meat; and put on the wound, if a hot abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if the fire has moved it, put on some ointments, until it is healed. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by bandages, then sew them together as I will say for wounds in the belly with stitches. 
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered to the bone and gaping, and does not hold together but only by a thread, sew it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat hearty meats, such as stewed beans and cooked wheat, as well as fowl and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.
