And if you find rotten flesh, and it does not reach the bone, sew up all the rotted part, and cut it away, then treat it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that bleeds freely, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it loose, tie it with thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy; it is that you put this powder on them so that they heal as the fire has moved them. 
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder subtly, and apply it to the wound, and remove it only when it has healed well and joined with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it unbound if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with quicklime alone when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the fire has moved the wound.  
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, immediately apply this powder to it; but put on some digested ointments or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it flows well; then continue other cures until it is healed.  
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with delicate forceps; and I will tell you about skull fractures later. 
de la plaie dou col	From the wound of the neck  
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes at the neck and it is simple, it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut. 
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and put nothing restrictive on it, for it will harm the nerves and cause them to retreat; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be under it, such as warm boiled chamomile flowers mixed with rose oil, and boiled comfrey also in lukewarm water, and other miner's stones according to this manner, and moist ointments. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed. 
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and raised and full of pus, pierce them lower; and if an artery is cut and blood flows, bind it and cauterize it; and if the spine of the throat is cut or the heart, and the conduit that carries the flesh is preserved, sew the heart onto the spine of the throat and do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural shape; then remove it carefully and leave it for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all that you can, and those that you cannot get, leave them until the wound rots and is freed and smoothed out its exit; and if the wound is fresh, apply powder onto the powder that I have mentioned. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter. 
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a spear or knife wound 
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a spear or knife and the wound is deep, see if the wound exhales putrefaction as the patient breathes: then know that the wound is mortal. And if it is not deep and fresh with all its blood, do not put powder in it the first hour nor bind it because of the blood which will not stop flowing completely, and return to the heart and kill the patient; but apply a drawing ointment and bind it twice a day. And if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days or four or more. If there is no spasm, nor tremor, nor pain in the heart, nor dislocations of the joints; and when you see these good signs, then know that the wound is saved. 
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with tents and other treatments as long as it is healing; and if it cannot heal, then know that there is a fistula; if the treatment is done as it should be. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, whether on the front, back, or side, then treat it as we have said before; if it is large, suture it; if it is small, use powder; and if it has penetrated into the bone and broken pieces, wash out the wound and treat the fractures if they are clean; and if they are not clean, let the wound rot so that the extraction will be easier; and for other wounds on other members, judgment is as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	for rupture of the belly 
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Ruptures of the belly are large, medium, and small; from a large wound, sometimes the intestines or nerves of the intestines protrude, allowing entry for others; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one because it is harder to put the intestines back in if they are not warmed one by one; because the intestines swell quickly when they feel cold and do not go back in as easily; therefore, a medium-sized wound is better because the intestines can be more easily returned to their place compared to others. And know that rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: the two common sutures occur in suturing the belly, and the sutures for other wounds on the body and the other two specific sutures are common with other wounds; but they are all cleaner with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and explain it.  
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines is outside, and it is easy to put back in place, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in the following way: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or you can cook in lukewarm water squinant and cypress and spikenard, and raise the intestines until the swelling is removed; and never do this using restraining bandages, but leave it loose so as to reduce the swelling. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestines with water or broth where almonds have been cooked, for this makes entry easier; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; the first dressing should be looser than the size of the wound, so that we do not cut except in cases of great necessity; and this is the instrument for cutting: cut inward at a curve and not outward, and look at this shape: 
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, if you can put it back in its natural form in its own place, then do so, for this is worthwhile. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, it is fitting that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, put his head and chest higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture from the belly is in one of the two sides, arrange it so that the injured side is higher than the other; and thus you should administer what I say in large and small wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, put what seems appropriate to you, then have in your hands a minister who holds the whole rupture with his hand, and bring together the lips; and this is the common way of stitching, and it is that you take one needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound a space of two finger widths, and put in a needle where there is strong thread; and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the fascia which is below the skin within, as far as you make it pierce that part, and bring together the two edges of the fascia together with the four. Then strain a double thread around the needle in two parts, then assemble the two edges of the wound evenly, then leave a space of two finger widths, and put in another needle; then tie the thread as you did for the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need needles, until the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium-sized, between subtle and large, because subtle needles cut through all the flesh, and those that are too large cannot enter well: therefore it is fitting that they are medium-sized; and do not put in the needles too far from the flesh and the skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; then cut the edges of the needles so that they do not bother the patient while sleeping, and place tents or cloths on the edges of the needles to hold them, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it suffices with one needle or two. The second stitch is common, and it is that you bring together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the fascia together on one needle where there is a medium-strong thread; and when you have pierced all these edges together, pull the needle back to where you started, in the way one sews linen cloths; and put a space between each stitch the thickness of half a finger width. This stitch heals the man well, and I stitched a wound on a man's belly or stomach which was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a handbreadth wide, and the intestines protruded two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up until the 15th day, and I treated it, and it was healed. 
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And those who saw him thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any ointment, because I was in a place where there was none, nor any medicine; and I put clean cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and put it through the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced straight through, take the head of the thread or cord where you put in the needle, and make it pierce through from the other side from the inside out; and the understanding of this suture is that you sew just as furriers sew furs, and you leave once the thread on one side, and pick it up again on the other, until the entire suture is complete.  
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of suturing, which Galen properly calls, is as follows: some assemble the two parts together naturally and join one end of the sinew to the other end in this way: put a needle or the end of a thread close by, and pierce only that place, leaving both ends of the sinew; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part to the inside, with both ends of the sinew; then pierce each one from the outside part to the inside, in two other ends of the sinew which are on the other side. And this is the gentler manner of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and some testify to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; and one must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than in other places of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of a wound is such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, so that the fire has moved it, then put back to air the intestines, and the cost; then put on powdered charcoal, and if the fire has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound swells; and stitch the thread, and let the sifac and the mirach be soldered; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to swell, old cotton, and stir it twice a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in several positions except when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will make commonality with the principal members, it is fitting that you moisten linen lightly in tempered oil, or in rose oil, and put it around the limbs, and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, then give enemas of warm red wine, and the same if the putrefaction comes up to the intestine; and pierce it within, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small ones. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the planting of the veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the vermiform appendix comes out of the wound, put it back in as soon as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, you must tie the place that is black so that blood does not flow into it, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligatures, and put the two ends hanging down from the part below the wound until the vermiform appendix comes out, and the wound heals. 
de la routure dou boueil	of a rupture of the eyeball 
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, one can restore it in some men, for I saw a man who was wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and there was excretion and flatulence; I treated it according to what I could, and did not cease to refine it until it was healed, and the edges were joined. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sutured, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he did not have any pain, but remained in better condition, and ate and drank; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this manner: take tweezers with large heads, then gather the edges of the wound, and when the tweezers have opened its mouth, put them on the two edges so that they tighten their mouths together; and then cut off the head, and this will hold so that it cannot be undone, then put another tweezer afterward in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These chiefs burn in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can bind the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of a beast, in this manner: take the head of this intestinal thread that is well-fleshed out, and then tie to the head of this thread a fine linen thread twisted together, then put the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine, and readjust it at the rupture; and this manner of suturing with tweezers is no other than according to the way of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the colon intestines, there is nothing but subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from a fistula or wherever it may be 
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes old, is universally called "fistula," and the same when it is raised and goes inward. 
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is, according to its greenness, a hard and white nodule where no pain is felt, and it is also raised like the feather of a bird; sometimes it has a clear opening inward, and sometimes thick; sometimes a little, and sometimes quite enough;  And as I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only because of one of nine causes: namely, by the smallness of blood or flesh; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or because there is too much pus; or because the wound is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality; or because the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is a type of pestilence; or because of the property in the region where digestion is late and healing, and it swells by nature; or because there are veins or bones. And I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is fitting that I make you know the cure of a fistula which is made by hand work. 
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all the members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if they extend to the principal property of the member, and similar things.  
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are hard to heal, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come up to the place I have said, and you are sure of the cure, and you see it known, if you take a tent of iron or linen, if the fistula is straight, so make it; and if the fistula is twisted, make it with a subtle tent of lead, for lead bends around the twisting; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well explore it by tents, then cauterize it through one of the openings, for moisture will pass from one opening to another, and it will cleanse it. Then cut the fistula freely at your power so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and remove all superfluity, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when pressing with his hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or from a nerve, or from an artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove all the corruption and bad humors that are within; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep and straight, then it is fitting that you cut deeply as much as you can, then put softened tents soaked in medicine in it, and push them to the bottom of the fistula, so that the medicine dissolves the superfluity which remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments that promote healthy flesh until it heals; and if it does not heal by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, cut it away.  
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not bother you or the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed and there is decay and blackness, cut away until all the decay is removed, then treat things that promote flesh healing until it is healed; and if it is not healed and returns to its former state, know that you are not going far enough: so uncover and scrape until you reach the bottom and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is nothing else to do but leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted and you can pull it out with forceps, extract it with an instrument suitable for this; and if there are many bones, extract them all, leaving none behind; and if moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear, cut through the moisture and flesh and free the bones.  
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something promoting decay on the wound and leave it until the pus is rotten around the bones, and then they will be removed more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, only raise the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part that is corrupted and comes up to the marrow of the bone, you must sew and cover everything up to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man of about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the humors went to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and he had no reason to open it; but the healers, in their folly, worked on it so much that they opened the abscess, and they corroded a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came many holes that all flowed pus and moisture from the body. And many healers treated him for about two years, and he had no knowledge of the art of hands, until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating it, and what was flowing through the holes to a great extent; and the young man's flesh became red, and he had a citrine color. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes, and I found that some came against each other from all sides of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then and cut into one of the holes until I uncovered part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption was coming up to the bone inside; I removed what appeared to me of the corrupted bone and thought that there was no other corruption, except for that which I removed; and I began to restore the wound with medicines that boiled for a long time, but could not solder it; and then I began again and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing into the bone, and I removed it, and then tried to solder the place; but I could not until I cut around a palm of the bone, and pierced it through its entire length, and then restored it with medicines; and it was healed and soldered quickly, and there was no need to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not suffer, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation often bled, but it was healed entirely, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, and was of good disposition and had neither harm nor any contrary at all, either coming or going. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it must be treated in this manner: take a linen thread and bind it to the head of the bone that appears, and command someone to stretch it upward; and put another woolen thread thicker than the first thread and tie it upon the flesh that is above the bone, and stretch the head so that you draw down the corrupted flesh below, and uncover the flesh upon the place where you wish to cauterize, so that the lye does not burn the flesh; and put a coal or a wooden board below the bone to prevent the burning of the corrupted flesh; and it must be treated as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and treated again another time. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh. 
dou feu	of fire 
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The flesh rots either from within or from without; and when you have medicine that corrodes by the cure of medicines, and it does not profit, then it is necessary to cut off that member up to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes death, or from malice, which is greater, from the defect of the member; and the signs are that the member becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corrosion goes from member to member, and takes over the whole body; if you hesitate to cut off, and if it is from the sting of some venomous beasts, such as a scorpion of the sea and viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the arm, then cut it off, and do not give it space to come up to the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, then cut it off at the joint so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut it off at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy except the amount of its virtue; and do the same when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut it off after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut off the whole foot; and if it rises into the leg, cut it off at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is nothing else to do but to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or sewing up the member is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister one of the ties down, and another minister the other tie up, and you sever the flesh which is between the two ties at a span wide, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or sew, and put a linen cloth on each side so that the sewing does not touch the healthy place, and causes the patient another injury and abscess. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you are working, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his left foot: he had a blackness that looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first came on the back of his left foot, spreading until it covered the whole foot; when the man saw the corrosion, he quickly decided to cut off his foot, and was healed; and long afterwards the corrosion returned to the back of his hand, and he came to me, and I put things that repel on him after cleansing the body, but could not stop the corrosions; and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's strength was weak; and he despaired entirely, and returned to his land, and quickly decided to cut off his hand, and was healed; and I do not tell this story except so that others may do the same, if they need to. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in fleshy places and stays so long that it gathers a great deal of pus; and then it bursts and the pus flows out, and the place remains empty, like a vessel; and the skin that is above is as delicate as linen cloth, and does not run down to the bone or to the nerve.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe that the flesh is burning, and the corruption is not complete, and the flesh is thick like leather, then cure it with a clyster thus: look whether the breast is large, and the bowel which comes from it has a foul odor, then give a clyster of Egyptian medicine which is made as follows: take alum, oil, and litharge equally, and put them to cook in a vessel over fire until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey; then take some of this according to your need, and make it into a liquid with water and honey, and give the clyster to the breast, and extract the pus; leave the medicine in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed; and never give a clyster of ash water when this medicine is not present, but take vine wood ashes, pour water on them, then strain it, and give the clyster with this, as long as you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then give a clyster of water and honey where there is a bit of powdered litharge; or you can give a clyster of honey and mead wine, so that the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the flesh grow; and when you have done this and believe that the breast is well cleansed, then give a clyster that produces flesh in it, and take diachylon plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine; or you can give a clyster of any medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken of their properties or treatise on ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small and the cannula of the clyster cannot enter, widen it a little with an iron instrument, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, sew it up and leave only one place where the clyster can enter; and if the opening that discharges pus is above, then move it lower down than it is. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowels are in perfect condition, do not let them fester with char; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see it, arrange it in such a way that the bowels run to the lowest place they are. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast swells with undigested food after many days, know that the breast does not clear. 
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons persist for a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches. 
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men in whom the healing of wounds is delayed, and some who do the opposite; and if undigested food swells in the breast after many days, know that the breast does not clear; and if the breast is slow to clear and is prolonged, apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diachylon ointment, for there is a great part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; take diachylon ointment and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance; then cook it and use it; and this same makes thickened honey better when diachylon ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind it, and sprinkle it on the honey when it is off the fire; and then in glue I wrap it and spread it on the breast, and sometimes I administer long aristolochia and roots of white lily, which are also like flour of beans and centaury; and use them either simply or compounded: grind them and make powder, and put them on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this cure, then know that corruption is perfect and makes an impression in the bone, or hard limbs, or joints; then treat the cure as a fistula, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger 
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Paronychia is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger or toe, or by chance it arises in other places; and when it is envied and one does not take heed, then it comes to a large abscess, and runs and discharges pus as much as it runs to the root of the nail, and by chance it runs all the way through; and it corrodes even to the bone, so that there comes a foul-smelling pain, and the flesh of the place is wide, and the color is dark red. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not profit, then it is fitting that you cut away all the superfluity that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.  
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses on the flesh, and begins to grow in, and the wound occurs, then it is fitting that you put a wedge under the nail that does not touch the flesh, and lift it up, and cut away this flesh subtly and lightly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines upon the remaining flesh to remove all of it; then treat it with ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut and treat it thoroughly, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see the bone corrupting, cut it in one of the ways described previously, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is hard, swollen, and he feels great pain, then you must first heal it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula, cutting across above it, and beware that the cut does not reach the flesh below the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on it that soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the deafness of the hand 
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The bone that grows in the hands of some men by chance is all fleshy, and sometimes it has part where it has bones, and sometimes it has a nail, and none others are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in some ways of the two bones. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those born without any marrow in the bone do not move, and those born at the joint of the bone may move; the size of one who is fleshy is light, in this manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those born at the root of the joint are difficult to heal; if you hold them, you must cut. 
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those born or who have no marrow at all, you must first cut the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for it, then treat it until it is healed. 
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joining that comes from the bones together comes by birth, or by the joining of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.  
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut that joining so that the bones rejoin according to their natural shapes; then put between two tents or cloths softened in rose oil so they do not join again; or you put between two pieces of soft lead, as long as its parts are joined, as it is appropriate.  
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to any of his limbs with the palm, then cover that swelling as it should be done. 
des vils	with warts 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large thick swollen full of melancholic superfluities, which come in many members of the body; and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others. 
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary for you to give him sometimes purging with colocynth, and then the juice of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is done in two ways: one is to cauterize them and draw out the black blood; and the other way is to tie off the vein and burn it completely. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The phlebotomy is done in this manner: first raise the leg with hot water very strongly, so that the thick blood becomes thin, then bind the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee; then cauterize the vein in one place or two or three places with a wide cut, then loosen and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one side to the other, as much as the strength of the patient can bear; and then bind it up and order him to abstain from meats containing black bile; and begin again the evacuation and the healing when the veins are full and harm the patient. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the arrow is according to this method: take the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs then shave it and put it in a bath, and apply hot water to the leg until it becomes red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, warm it by the fire and then cut the skin at the vein's length from the top of the knee, or in the lower part below the ankle; then loosen the skin with an incision, and flay the vein on all sides until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black and when it enters into the skin it seems like a white cord; then put the arrow beneath, as long as it is raised from the skin and then tie it lightly to an incision, then cut it in another place above III times; then flay the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with the arrow, as you did, and tie it at another incision as you did first; then cut another size or several if you need them, then lift it, and tie it to the toe's joint, then draw and lift it up to the second size; then pull it out from size to size until it is all free, then tie it; and if you cannot draw and raise it, insert a needle at the whole strong thread doubled, tie it, and draw it; and insert it below the arrow and turn your hand back and forth on both sides until it comes out; and be careful that it does not cut, for if it cuts, one cannot draw or lift it and it harms the patient; and when you have drawn all of it out, put wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and treat it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cut it; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein must be curved and not sharp so that it does not cut the vein; and it is of a large curve because if it were slender, it would cut the vein but it must be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:  
de la voinne civile	of the civilian vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it may grow elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the rot that comes from under the skin, as snakes and worms come within the body, embedded between the skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes color, and begins to come out forcefully, like the root of a plant. 
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the head opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of linen from three and a half to ten fingers long, tie it off, and leave the linen hanging on the leg; and every time it sticks out at the end, wrap it around the linen, and tie it off; and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap up the rest, and do not cut it off at its root as long as it has all come out; for if you cut it off, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and rot or pus and evil disease; so for this reason, it is necessary that it be treated bit by bit until the very end, and nothing remains of it or any flesh; and there are times when this vein, when it is treated, is ten palms long, or even twenty; and one man came to me whose was twenty palms long; and when you cut it off, it spurts out one ray or hole, and pierce it through to the bottom so that everything comes out; and let the matter which is inside be emptied, and apply to the place medicines that prevent putrefaction any day, then treat it as abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never at this vein with less than four rain (drops), and the same when it opens in the joint of the foot or leg, there comes much pus, and from which it leaps rain; cure it then as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "beef disease," because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and one feels it well from limb to limb, as long as it tears the skin where it goes, and leaps far; and it arises from putrefaction of certain humors, as come worms and serpents and lampreys and ascarides or belly; and one doubts its harm, for when it goes through the body and mounts to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it heal and drain, one cannot cut except when it goes; so it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong tight band, then cut on it and draw out the pus, and if the worm is completely embedded in the flesh and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it runs to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the eye, remove the eyebrow underneath it, then cut on it and draw out the pus; and it is necessary to use the patient for cleansing of the body with soluble medicines for bad rotten humors, and beware of meats causing putrefaction. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vacating," and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and a little while after, I saw it rise as like a worm on her shoulder, more quickly than anything else, as like living silver when it cuts from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and stuck in her shoulder, and then a little while after ran through all her body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it was turning around her body again, just as I saw. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner. 
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.
