However, I had seen many who had felt pain move from one place to another, but I had never seen it as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins, and therefore this constrained windiness appeared; and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are fleshy, and who have moist bodies and filled veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see curing this disease, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, bind it above and below quickly, and then cauterize on top until this windiness constrained at the place is forced out; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it in your eyes, so cure it with those that expel windiness, such as fetid pills, and serpent pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearances and according to the places in bodies where they fall.  
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are some which have large points, and small ones, and barbed ones, and fletched ones; and some which have two angles, and some which have wings, and some which have pieces; and those which fall in any limb fall according to two manners: either in a principal member such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.  
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the head is in any place of these limbs and the sign of death which I will tell you later appears to you: then it is necessary that you beware of extracting this arrow for death comes afterwards in many situations; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not embedded perfectly, then treat it and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow is lodged and pierces the bone, and the dura mater which is above the brain swells, is when there is darkness and stupor and greenness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it occurs without pus from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and there comes moisture white looking like pus from the wound, and burning also like fire from a chariot; and if these signs appear to you, then keep away from treatment and treat the arrow if it is not embedded. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of a stroke when it strikes the heart is that it is near the left breast, and also feels as though it were fixed in something hard, not empty; and by chance the stroke moves just like a pulse, and there comes black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt that death approaches. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that has not gone all the way through is that without any foam, pus comes from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs heavily and wants cold air. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes in the covering of the bladder, it is below the ribs; and there comes great anguish and great pain and sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulders move. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, it may happen that undigested food comes from the wound. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow lodges in the gut, and there is no sign of it passing through the intestines, there is no hope for a cure or extraction of the arrow. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow lodges in the bladder, and the urine comes out with force, and the patient feels intense pain: know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and shoulder blade and spine of the back and forearm and thigh and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various positions. 
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me so that you do otherwise. 
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell or lodged near the root of his nose: I tried it, and drew it out from the other side below the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any harm. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And draw out with one game an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye beneath the skin below, and the arrow was filled, and could only reach its point towards the fire, and it was an arrow as large as a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; the game was cured, and no evil accident befell him. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arab arrow with ears; I shaved the beard, and manipulated it so skillfully that I drew it out, and the Christian was cured. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I drew an arrow from a man, which had fallen into his belly, and thought he would die; and then after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow and splinted it, and drew it out forcefully, and he did not suffer any ill effects.  
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man who has an arrow lodged in his back or chest, and the wound has healed over it; and the arrow remains inside him and does not change its natural position, and he experiences no harm in any of his natural functions. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you see another man who has an arrow lodged in his face, and the wound has healed over it; and it remains thus causing great pain; and many other similar cases. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow wound for the king's nephew, which was lodged between his nostrils and inclined towards the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called to treat him three days after it had been lodged.  
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it carefully with a subtle instrument, and did not feel any resistance; and he felt numbness and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of an arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on the plaster for four days and sewed up the wound properly and kept the patient long time until he felt the arrow one day inside his flesh and told me so. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound medicine sharp and corrosive for four days until it opened, and I probed and felt the head of the arrow moving in its place; then I added to the opening of the wound by that sharp medicine until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and after passing well the limits around four months, then enlarged so the wound that I put in the forceps, and moved it from one side and the other, but could not get it out; then I did not cease to refine and contrive various ways and instruments until I took it one day with forceps well made, according to its form which will be seen at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the master judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say, because books cannot contain everything; but wise masters compare much with a very small thing, and with what is present and lacking, they find nine works, and nine instruments, for removing foreign objects that occur in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of the limbs where they are lodged except according to two manners: either through the place where they entered, or through another part; and the one which comes out further through the place where it entered is an arrow entering into flesh, and this happens very rarely now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it stay until the flesh around it is rotten and the exit is widened; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it every day; and then it will come out. And if it does not come out, pierce around it with a thin awl, until the flesh around it is enlarged, and then remove it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the skull, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: do not remove it, but leave it until it becomes equal after several days, for if the arrow reaches the sinus, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not reach the sinus, and the patient remains for several days without any bad accidents, then begin the removal. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck like that and cannot come out by force, then administer bandages around it, as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in a place in the body so that it cannot be seen, probe for it with your whole finger; and if you feel it, remove it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, enlarge the wound until it is big enough; and remove the arrow if you can, and if there are ears on the arrow to which it clings, cut the flesh that is stuck around it in two places so that you can move it, then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; be careful not to break the arrow so that you could pull it out more easily.  
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding flesh is rotten, then treat it, for the extraction will be easier. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then apply what we have said about treating it in its chapter; and beware of cutting a nerve or vein, and try to draw out the arrow as best you can, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient as they were when the arrow fell upon them, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then place them according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	An arrow that has entered from another side, where you perceive nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in a place where one can see or feel it apparently: cut then until the forceps can grasp it, and then extract it; if it jumps out now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out. 
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then begin the extraction again until it comes out forcefully; and if it were from an arrow, push it all the way through; and if it were bone, and you see that forceful pushing is needed, use a tool with a pointed end, so that the point of the arrow enters the groove of the tool; and then push forcefully, and if the arrow is barbed, push the tool with its point entering inward, to make the extraction easier. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow sticks in the flesh or the chest or the belly or the bladder or the ribs, and it is close by, and you can cover it up, then do so; and beware of covering a vein and a nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary; and care for it until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one treats arrows resembles the beak of a bird, and see here for its shape:  
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pushing end is also like the feather of a bird, to push on the point of the arrow, as here is its shape: 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the forceps for pushing and pulling is this: 
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins in the body 
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins in which one can bleed, of which there are sixteen on the head: to know, two arteries that are behind the ears, called the "two herbch"; and two arteries which are at the two temples appearing; and two veins which are at the two corners of the two eyes, which are called "aspirers"; and a vein located in the middle of the forehead; and a vein on the top of the head; and two cords that are at the neck; and two veins which are above the lips over the mouth, these being the veins called "augeherich"; and two veins below the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and common people call it the "head vein"; and the middle one is called the "fascia," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilica, and common people call it the "heart vein"; and the basilica is on the right side, and common people call it the "belly vein," and it is above the fossa, and it is the one from which blood is drawn, which appears distinctly above the pouch.  
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvation vein is the one that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the pouch on the left side, and the second saphenous vein is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The cutting of the veins that are after the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines; and the qualities of the bloodletting, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's collar with a screw, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two hanging strands from the head: hold them to your thumb, and where you feel the pulse below your thumb, that is the sign to cut; then take the lancet, and put it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the whole vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein well two lengths across, and let blood out as much as you see; then bind and tie, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for old migraines, and those that are habitual, and accustomed ophthalmia, and for the body of sharp tears at the eyes; and the quality of the bleeding is as I say: and it is that the patient tightens his neck, so that the two veins appear openly; and he feels the thumb under his finger, and then squeezes with a grip; then lifts the heart above the vein at the top with his index finger, and puts the lancet below, and lifts the vein above, and cuts it, as you have done in the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then bind it with a bandage, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of them and their cutting and their extraction, at the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the bloodletting of the cephalic for old facial illnesses, and migraines, and redness; and its quality is that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose form is this: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then untie the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and never again open it with a wide flame.  
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not fitting that the flame be too strong; and bloodletting across, for the bone is nearby, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle. 
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Bloodletting of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts helps for eye ailments, and itching, and redness, and oriel in the eye, and facial illnesses; and the quality of their bloodletting is that the patient twists his neck with any ligature, as before; then bleed, and whether the bleeding is across, a prick a length of a flame a prick wide, for there is no flesh.  
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, it may break by chance; then make a run of blood, as much as you need, and then tie it with cotton, and tie it well. 
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bloodletting from the vein of the nose is good for ague, and for strong fevers, and for diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that comes to the face, even when it is old; and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient pinches his neck, then strains his nose with your left hand, and takes a long subtle flame, and puts it between the lip in the space which is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not go too far into perfection, and make the blood flow according to your need, then tie it up for one night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bloodletting of two veins helps with the tightening of the groin, and at the beginning of melancholy, and for many diseases, and for scabies, and for corroding, and for herpes, and for estimenses; and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient stretches his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then bleed the vein for a long time broadly, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as is needed; then redo it in the other vein, then untie the cord, and loosen all the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave him until morning, so that the wound may heal. 
de la sainie des leivres	Of the bloodletting of the veins 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting of the veins above the lips helps with boils in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and nosebleeds and toothache. 
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the vein is such that it makes the patient sit in front of you, and remove their collar as I have said; then turn back the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them are small black veins: therefore take one and the other, and if you do not know them, and are in doubt, take the largest of each side, and do the same for the two veins which are above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein below the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The vein below the tongue helps after the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and eye diseases, and mouth diseases; and the quality of the phlebotomist is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks underneath on each side a black vein: therefore cut one and the other, and do not go too deep, because below are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins from which we commonly bleed are bled in two ways: either by pricking with a wide-bladed lancet or with a delicate olive-shaped one, as thin as a cutting needle, and called "anesil"; and they are wide and delicate according to the width and narrowness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the wide lancet is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see: 
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary for opening the raised veins full of thick blood that appears, and which contain thick and cloudy blood; and this is the shape of the olive-shaped lancet: 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the delicate veins, where there is subtle citric blood. 
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses that are below the throat, and at the neck, and at the chest, and at the belly; and it is fitting for the bleeder that he bleed moderately, and that he beware of the artery that is below. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the artery, and bleeding comes, then it must be cauterized as I have said; and the flame should not be piercing, but cutting like a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, then you must remove it and change to another; or if you want no blood from it, then you place a vein in its place on the arm: it opens clearly; and cut it with a knife blade as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the vein, then it is fitting that you remove the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with ink, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with a knife blade; and be careful not to strike the artery when you see the place swell, for that is an artery: avoid it then. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding upwards just like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery: hurry then, and place your finger on it lengthwise, then remove your finger if the blood stops flowing; for many times this happens; if it bleeds, bind the arm and leave it as such, and do not let the patient move it; and be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it comes to you, and medicine is not present to you, then bind the artery so that it closes, for the head of the artery will retract; and stop the blood. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of elder bark, and split it, and take one half and tie it on well until the next day; if the blood stops, that is good; if not, then treat it as we have said with powders that stop blood flow; and the stopping should be done gently in several positions because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the bandage on the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the middle arm aids so much that it draws blood from above the head and below the body, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it behoves the healer to be cautious for the nerve which is beneath, and if he points too sharply, and finds the nerve, it swells and the healing is spoiled, and perhaps it cannot heal; and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men because of its subtlety, then you must heal it with an instrument without anesthesia; and avoid the nerve as best you can. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then he should make it long. 
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the cephalic aids so that it draws blood from the head and helps these; and it behoves to heal with a pointed olivewood or myrtlewood instrument, for it is the safest of all veins, because there is neither nerve nor artery beneath. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to find the lightest place, and do not be upset if one must try the first time, and begin again; and by chance, some men's limbs swell when one tries the first time, but this does not matter. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the incision is according to your thought. 
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know about bleeding is that it is not administered except to maintain health and to avoid future diseases; and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins which are: the cephalic, basilic, and median cubital; and it should be done at the beginning of spring in youth, and in autumn and winter after eating when signs of repletion appear; and it should be done on the first day or the third, after two hours or three from the day. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting that is administered to the sick has no determined hour, but only when need is in the day or the night, at all hours and at all times; and it is not fitting to bleed children until fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying a fetus before the fourth month until the seventh.  
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should one bleed those who are old and have passed sixty years. 
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, it is fitting that they cleanse their bowels with a light clyster, if they have retained much phlegm, so that the veins do not draw from the bowels harmful superfluities injurious to the principal members; nor should one who is too full of meats bleed, nor one who is drunk, as long as they are inebriated, nor those suffering from dropsy; and one should avoid bleeding after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse with a woman, or labor, watching, fasting, and those whose virtue has been depleted by something from the arm or body. Then, if the blood is thick, thin it with foods and drinks and medicines if you have them; then take a bath, if nothing forbids it, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein of the left wrist near the third hour, as we have said. And refrain on that day from work, exertion, luxury, and similar things; be calm and joyous, and let the bleeder stand higher than the one being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then loosen the ligature moderately, for if it is too tight or loose, blood will not flow. Then rub the spot with your hands until the veins swell and you feel them; then moisten the blade with a drop of old oil, then place the thumb of your left hand under the spot where you wish to bleed, so that the vein does not move when cut.  
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee as quickly as cords in a stringed instrument, and some of these are full of windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it withdraws from the flame and cannot open the vein, and so is it with this; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary that the bloodletters be aware in these matters. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, one begins again a little below that place or above hastily, if the veins are not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are swollen and the patient is afraid, leave them for one or two days and do not bind the arm: perhaps abscesses will come; do not enter a bath, then begin the bloodletting again if it pleases him; and if the puncture is small, or the vein is thin, subtly cut it and you doubt that as much blood as you see will not come out, apply all the flame directly to that puncture itself; and work quickly, so that the veins are swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not begin the lancing again, and put a poultice of oil upon it, for it draws out the blood from the body, and is softened in this place by the oil; and thus administer the oil poultice in every vein that you lance to stop the flow of blood; and this same does triacle and wine when it is put on the place; if too subtle the blood spreads and parts when it is too large. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, even when it has not been lanced more than this time when the opening of the vein is small, hurry and put upon the place a sponge moistened in hot water and leave it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood issues from the vein, and if it remains at the place after some days without any blackness or greenness, do not harm it; and if you see, put on some aloes or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, costmary, or something similar.  
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there appears an abscess and swelling at the vein of the basilary artery; put then your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of your hand, that is the bad swelling. 
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be careful that you do not put anything of what we have said on it, for by chance you may cut the artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed. 
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And give each blood according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood. 
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow out until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down. 
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for those who are full and strong, and need bloodletting, that a wider incision be made, and the flames be wide; and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and they should be bled often in small amounts, and one should bleed them by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from the flow of blood and the cutting of nerves, and is worth more than a long or wide incision.  
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body lacks blood, it is fitting to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is feverish, draw blood three or four times. And if he is of a cold complexion, before the bleeding give softened bread in thickened syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-scented syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the bleeding, after a large amount of blood is let, it is fitting that he inhale broth of flesh and subtle scented syrup, and use the other things we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for evacuating the veins. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed his arm again, and bleed another time, it is fitting that when he is weakened by a great bleeding, that he should bleed a little at a time, according to the quantity of his continuing strength. 
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to bandage his arm after the first cauterization, and he has strong flesh, should cauterize seven hours after the first cauterization, or after the ninth hour. 
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to cauterize another area, should do so on the second day or the third. 
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that has already been heated, and it brings fever; so it is necessary to draw a great quantity, and widen the opening as much as it will let out pus; then when you have fulfilled all the conditions of cauterization, place your hand on his pulse while he is being cauterized, so that death does not come in place of pus, and this happens many times when the cauterizer is negligent; and it is not fitting when you see the arm being loosened, and making blood issue a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly upon it; nor if it is crooked, should he extend his arm hastily, for that would be bad; but let him leave it until it has been cauterized the second time; or you point the tip of the flame, so long as the blood which is frozen at the opening of the vein comes out freely, and place a small piece of linen sharpened to a point, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess is calmed. 
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a need to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm. 
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein near the elbow is healthier to draw from than the vein at the temple because it is more substantial.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bloodletting is this: the patient puts their hand in warm water until the forearm is red; then it is tied moderately so that the vein appears well, and then the bloodletting is done crosswise, not lengthwise or wide; and the opening should be wide, and the bloodletting should be done very close to the joint of the hand, and if none comes out, put the hand back in warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in warm water again, for it is used more in winter than in summer; and the bloodletting of this vein is safer than all other veins because there is no artery or nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sinew of the salvation of the right hand is worth against all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and plunge it in hot water, as long as the vein becomes swollen, if you see it; and if the sinew is across, and if you cut it altogether, it does not matter; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are beneath all naked of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the sinew is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn off as much blood as needed, put oil and wax on the vein to heal quickly, and do this for every vein.  
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sinew in the left hand is good against the illness of the mouse, and do everything as I told you about the right. 
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The venom of the viper is good for all illnesses that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the thighs and old legs, and similar illnesses. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its venom is such that the sick person puts their foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it bursts, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there are many veins; therefore choose a wider vein, or one at the ankle, which is better. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you choose it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and let the venom flow as in cutting, and let the flames be extinguished. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the venom cannot come out, put the foot back in hot water and let the vein drain well. 
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the sinews fail the first time, start again the second time a little higher, because the flesh is salty; and do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same to the sinew of the other foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the ankle strong, and its sinew is worth the pain of the hip, when it is for hot blood. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its sinew is such that the patient enters or bathes, and squeezes above the ankle four times in twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, draw the sinew in all the ways you can, and across; and it is worth drawing until you tire, because the flesh is underneath, and it is very full in most men. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, draw any vein of his that opens or the back of both feet, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and draw as much blood as you see, and then untie the ligature, and put cotton on top and remove it; it is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	from cupping glasses 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or of glass, or of wood; and cupping is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking. 
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done without pricking is done in two ways: either with heat, or without heat; and cupping which is done by pricking and extraction of blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is all along the top of the head; and another around the neck; and two others on both sides of the neck; and a cupping glass under the chin; and a cupping glass on each shoulder; and a cupping glass on the buttocks; and cupping glasses down both arms; and cupping glasses down both legs; and cupping glasses on both ankles; and this cupping does not draw blood, except for small veins which are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone as much as one does by bleeding a vein; and it is not fitting that it be administered, either with heat or without heat, in any disease which comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness it is required to cup, or by custom, we will administer them each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between; for there are some who when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; and there are some who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swelling of the tongue, and spit blood; and there are some who faint, and see by night blood and sadness and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and immediately it is the middle of the month, we order them not to be cupped after three hours of the day. 
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The remedy of the leech helps with the headache... which comes to them, and it is not fitting that this be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this cupping is in place of the remedy of the cephalic vein, and it is not fitting that he who has a cold complexion use it, or who has diarrhea, for this does them great harm; and therefore it is not fitting that the elderly use it, nor those with head colds.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become stiff, and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass a bit lower due to the risk of stiffness. 
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping on the neck is in place of the sinews of the head and the basilisk vein, and for this reason it is good for constriction of the breast, and a fissure in the canal of the diaphragm, and all things, and repletion; and it must be applied lightly, for if it holds too tightly, it will cause stiffness or stomach and heart ailments. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping on the second ribs of the neck is good for headaches, ophthalmia and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of teeth, and it is in place of the sinew of the basilisk vein; and you must instruct the patient to express his hand while placing it, so that he does not press on the artery, and cause a flow of blood.  
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Cupping below the chin is good for mouth disease, and gum decay, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is placed on the two lips. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping on the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and swelling. 
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Cupping on the elbows is as good as three veins in the arms, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the healer not to make too strong a suction, for the flesh is thin there, and under it are nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping that is on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids in the bottom, and for illnesses below, and it is fitting that the cupping be large, and be made of horn, so that it can draw well; and by chance, if it were delicate, it would break; and it would make large wounds. 
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	If the cupping glasses on the legs bleed freely, for they draw blood from all over the body, and are good for old pains of the joints, and of the bladder, and soften swellings; and are placed at the two shins, and the two ankles, but they weaken the body after long use, and bring pallor in many constitutions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on a cupping glass is that you first put it empty, and suck temperately, and apply it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the place red and swollen, and you see the redness of the blood; then remove it, and replace the cupping glasses, and take heed in the constitution of bodies, for there are some who have soft flesh, and clear pores: so it is fitting to apply it once only, and it is fitting to make wide wounds, and a deep prick; and suck gently. 
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice; the first time to thin the way of the thick blood. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only strike once. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we start often; and if the blood is thick, we strike deeply enough so that the heart is pierced only slightly, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have many pores, that you moisten the cups with oil which is stimulating and dissolving: if it is summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is winter, with watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or other similar ones. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsamite, or oil of anise, and the like. 
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one whom we are healing has delicate flesh and large pores, it is not fitting to put any oil on, but rather wash after the ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of gourd, or water of porcelain, or other like. 
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them rise with water of ash, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and the like things.  
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities let them rise with old wine, or water of vinegar, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or others like; and it is not fitting to heal with a cupping glass before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the ventosation, and it is fitting that he wash himself, when he is about to be cupped and when he has been cupped.  
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware that he who heals is choleric, and if the flesh is too hot and inflamed; it is fitting that he takes cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce in season, and similar things; and eats little, and meat of a young pig, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and moderately spiced wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat piglets and small birds and pigeons; and on the day that he will have himself cupped, he should drink more than he eats; and it is fitting to give some men sometimes triacle or musk before or after cupping, to strengthen the principal limbs; and let the flesh be subtle, but it does not suit those who are hot to drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Cupping glasses that are put without cutting are those that are put on the liver, and on the thighs, and gout, and on the belly and buttocks and loins and hip; for these limbs do not suffer to be cut, and we only do it to draw blood from limb to limb, such as we put on the breasts when a newborn is unwell; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, such as we put cupping glasses on the belly and buttocks to soften the limb; and to remove pain, when there is opilation or stone, its attractive virtue may by chance remove the opilation, or loosen the stone from its place; and so it does when we put it on the liver and thighs when there is retained windiness; and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in diseases of pleurisy; and in this way one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for it have been cooked. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass applied with fire is thus: 
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.
