And it has two widths and half a palm in diameter, and it has on its side near the middle one small hole, as for inserting a needle, and it should be of iron, smooth in front so that it does not scratch the patient when placed upon the limb; and it has in the middle a crossbar of iron or wood, for placing a lighted candle, and there are both large and small ones according to the illnesses and the age of those who use them; for cupping glasses for children are different than those for old people, and those for thin people are different than those for fat people. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must apply this cupping glass to the limb thus: take the candlewick of wax or linen thread, and put it through the cupping glass through the crossbar that is in the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, with its two ends over the hole that we have mentioned, so that when you want to see if the vapor goes, remove the cupping glass; and take the linen thread as before, and start again often, if you need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered for pleurisy, in all acute conditions, it has neither stalk nor perforation and is not applied unless it is full of water, and it is placed upon the limb only; and this is its form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping glasses are not applied unless in limbs where one cannot place cupping glasses because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in these parts devoid of flesh, such as veins or noses, and other similar ones; and the quality of the user is such that when you find cupping glasses which are in fresh sweet water without rust, you take them; and put them one night in fresh water, until they become familiar, and have nothing inside; then let them be cleansed with a vein and a cupping glass, then rub the limb so that it becomes red, and place the cupping glasses on top of it; and when they are full and stick, if it is a place where one can put a cupping glass, then put it on, because this is worth much afterwards. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this is not the case, lift it gently first and then sharply, very well, and then inhale deeply. And if the veins are too close to the body's flesh, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put it on top until the veins shrink; and if the veins are multiplied, put crushed vitriol or alum and similar things on top until they shrink; then you put half the peeled beans on the spot and leave them there until they burn at the spot, which will stop it now; and if you need more, take other veins. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins do not want to be taken, rub the area with fresh blood, or insert a needle into it until the vein emerges, and then put them on top; as soon as they feel the blood, they will burn; and when you see that they are falling off, sprinkle a pinch of powdered aloes and salt, or ashes, and they will fall off now. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures 
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations. 
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the folly of men is to think that they have seen everything in this chapter, for they have never seen any of the old books, nor read a single letter; and because of this, the science is foreign in our land, for I have never found any good one; and I do not know anything except through the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in these two chapters before.  
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is fitting then that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of speech and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and he remains on truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others. 
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is fitting that you hurry to heal the sick person on one side and the other, if nothing hinders him, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if his time is very short, or too cold; and forbid cold foods, that is to say cold meats, and flesh of fowl and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill oneself too much with foods which fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess, nor spreading of matter in the limb; if the sick person returns to his former government that he used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with meats that produce great nourishment, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in broth, rice, and pies, and cow's stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things. 
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with good nourishment the muscles are recovered and the break heals sooner. 
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well rejoined or soldered according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those which are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, set the broken bone with strong bandages that hold it tight and join the limb together, until it is strengthened as it was before; and do not move it at all from its place, and for this reason, it is necessary to nourish it with large meats, as we have said.  
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways. 
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures. 
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to splintering, and another in sharpening, like the point of a pen for writing. 
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small crack all the way through.  
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own treatment and instrument for restoration according to what the memory brings back to its place; and a fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted and clearly seen upon touching; it also sounds under pressure from the hand; and when there is no twisting nor sound upon touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there may well be twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.  
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not fitting that you move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come afterward, and then extract it now subtly. 
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that for a fracture which goes awry, and are the two parts separated, it is fitting now to put them back together equally, just as abscesses come to life; and if abscesses come hot, leave them for a day, until the abscess is appeased; then put it in line with what you can lightly and wisely move, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of those where there are pieces; then extract it, as it is fitting afterward. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone has two broken parts, whether it is hand or foot, or in your hand it is a small limb, or with two cords, or one cord and in your hand; and set the limb according to its natural shape so that when the parts of the broken limb are freed, then reset by all means the additions in their places as you can, and make sure that through your work there comes neither injury nor pain to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.  
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: if it straightens nicely, and do not hold it too tightly, do not press as those who cause an abscess and contraction of the limb by their work, as we have often seen. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, chastise the patient well so that he does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other way; and ensure well that the limb is so secure that he does not feel any pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels any pain, it is not in place, and you must put it in a position where he feels no pain; and make sure that it is placed straight so that crookedness does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in size and shape. 
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and wrists and similar ones; it is fitting to wrap them with soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs; it is fitting to wrap them with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the whole large limb, and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no mark; then tie around splints of light wood, three turns or four according to the limb, and restrain your hand one span along the whole bandage, then go above the fracture and restrain it less, so that the fracture then moves a span away from the fracture; and soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy place, then take the other bandage and turn around again on the fractured place; then return to the part below the fracture, and restrain it moderately, not too strongly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above; then put between the bandages splints of linen or cloths, until they are all equal, then tie everything together with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something soothing on the hot abscess, and that removes the swelling, and leave it like that for several days; then strain it with your splints, and they should be half the width of a cane sharpened at one end, or from wood used to make wedges, or from palm leaves, and be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as is appropriate for the size of the limb, whether small or large; then strain it with the splints as you did in the first place, then tie a thread on top evenly, as in the first place on the fracture; narrower on one end, looser on the other; and it is necessary that the threads be medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in some works by fools who make their bandages with twisted linen thread, this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and it is not right that there should be less than two fingers' space between each splint. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is bruised by the head of the bone after tightening in their joints, then put bandages of linen or wool fleece beneath them so that they do not bleed. 
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture and the heart is broken, I will tell its cure hereafter. 
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not suit to set all the broken limbs on the first day.  
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it does not suit to set the bones forcefully before five or seven days, or more according to your judgment of the hot abscesses that appear; and see here the manner of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsion: and it is that you take flour that stays at the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster restoring the fracture in many positions, and likewise for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.  
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three bay leaves and ladani and enula and asafetida and gum arabic and mugwort, each ten drachmas; myrrh and aloes, each five drachmas; alchechil nine drachmas; and make powder, and mix them with the white of an egg. If the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and it is worth more to many men. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plaster that is worth for torsion: take mugwort and vismalve, each ten drachmas; myrrh and aloes, each nine drachmas; acace six drachmas; Armenian bole ten drachmas, and grind well, and confect with water or white of egg, and administer. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way of plaster for joints and bones separated from their places, and soothes the pain arising, and uses it to cut the bone, and the fracture: take new wool, and moisten it in lye and boiled oil, and put on the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for calming a hot abscess, and properly removes the pains. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make a plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and common poppy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make a plaster for the restoration of a broken bone and to soften the remainder of an abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take marshmallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, of each one part; and grind them, and mix with wine, and if the member is inflamed, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make a plaster stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes for the restoration of the limb. 
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take marshmallow root, flaxseed, elecampane, melilot, and sanicle, and violet flowers and chamomile flowers, of all an equal part; and grind them, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to restore strength except for cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else besides, and he says it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard. 
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that one should put on a broken limb, to restore it, dry things a bit warm, such as myrrh and aloe and frankincense and similar things, as we have said. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of poultice that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and horsehair chopped up, or bird feathers, and agrimony, and grind them equally, and make a poultice and bind it. 
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then untie it a bit afterward, and take care that the patient feels no pain, and that the bone does not move from its place; if so, do not untie it for several days. And if pain comes to the area, or itching, or discomfort or swelling, then hasten, and untie it, and remove the poultice now; and take a light cloth, and a damp sea sponge, and plunge it in water, and lift the area, until the itching stops and the pain is eased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry wool soaked in water or rose oil on top, and bind it overnight, until you are sure of a warm abscess; and ease the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then start again the gentle binding, and a bit of poultice, and do not strain it as hard as before; and continue gently until it is healed. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess has drained and is red, painful, and swollen, and all the pus has been removed, and you need plaster and bandages, if it starts again as you did at first, equally so. 
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, do not untie it except after III days or IIII or V or VII; and never leave it for XX days, according to what you see, as long as the fracture heals, and the adjustment of the flesh approaches above; then restrain it more than at first, and thicken its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see the place dry more than necessary, know that no nourishment can come there; apply then a bandage soaked in hot water every time you untie it, and this be every third day, and leave a hole at the wound; by this work therefore, you cut off nourishment to the limb, and quickly amend what the foolish surgeon has done, who leaves the limb twisted: this is bad, and it is dangerous work, and I see nothing else but to let go and work straight.  
des diverses manieres de brisure	of diverse kinds of breaks 
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of breaks and diverse figures, and the causes are predetermined; for there are breaks that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck bone shatters all the bone up to the tissue which is below the bone, as a hatchet or club does; and for this reason this manner of break is called "haichure." 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone above without piercing it, and this manner of break is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two breaks is large or small. 
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or fissure or neck bone from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or other similar things. 
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating break, which approaches up to the tissue which is below the bone, or it is upon the bone, and this wound is either large or small. 
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound is rejoined to the bone as fine as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and causes the piece of bone to enter inwards, and the edges are chewed up like smiths do when they strike upon anvils; if the stone enters within. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have soft or moist bones, such as the skull of a child; and it happens in all these ways of fracture that small pieces are detached like tiles; and I will speak of them in their place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the traction upon them, and the inquisition into the wounds, and by the corrupted flesh which is upon them. 
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	A similar hair is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs gently upon it, if the fracture appears black. 
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, pay attention to the accidents of the patient, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting bile, and loss of understanding, and spasm, and pallor, and fever ague, and the eyes coming out strong and red, and other similar things in many dispositions, then it cannot be healed without doubt. 
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a worrying accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment. 
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it is fitting to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the time that you can. 
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone becomes corrupted, and accidents come which we have said. 
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the web that covers the brain, it is fitting that you split the split part thus: and take hold of the head of the patient firmly, and uncover on the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more often than you can, and if discharge of blood comes at uncovering the bone, or an abscess rises, help it with what is fitting, and fill the place with cloths softened in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the risen abscess is calmed, and be sure of discharge of blood; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two manners of work: one manner if you cut at a narrow cut in front, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I make another cut larger than the first. 
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of different sized blades, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are made of hardened iron; and in work lightly so that you do not bruise the head. 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you administer cuts with trephines, not too deeply so that they do not penetrate beyond the bone of the skull, and the point must have a margin or a circle above it, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of them, so that each one comes in its place depending on the type of bone, so that you have trephines for all types; and this is the form of the three types of trephines: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place the trephine on the bone and turn it between your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then put the trephine elsewhere a bit afterward, and do this all around, then cut with scissors the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain nor the dura mater. 
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and removed it, it is fitting that you leave the tool which remained from the bone to all the other instruments similar to an incisor, but it is fitting that it be finer and more subtle than the other incisor; and if any of the small bones or scales remain, remove them lightly with the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and dressings as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is that which Galien says, which is safer and he praises it greatly, and this is his word. 
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is fitting that you uncover a part of the bone where the fracture appears most open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you place under the head of this lenticular incisor, which has this shape: 
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting edge is toward the bone; then strike with a small mallet on it, so that you gently chip away at the bone all around, and be well aware of the cloth which is underneath; if it touches the bone, remove the bone lightly, for one can remove it safely without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate as far as the cloth, and the bone is cut only on top, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to scrape away that roughness, and remove the flakes with a delicate razor, of which you must have various sizes, in order to administer the most suitable one, according to the work and the shape of the fracture. 
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you begin with large razors, and then use more delicate ones, and do not cease doing so until it is well done. 
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you administer according to its direction; and this is something that is not answered to one who has put his study in this art. 
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the syfac is uncovered, it is necessary that you take a linen bandage, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another bandage doubled into two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first bandage; and do this as lightly as you can so that you do not weigh down the syfac, then administer another bandage on top, and do not tighten it too hard, only so that it holds the wound; and leave it like this for one or two days, until the abscess has calmed down, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristoloche, and similar things; and make a powder of these things and put them on the wound, and then administer cleansing medicines without biting, and ensure that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave any ointment there, nor allow pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the cloth covering the brain, it will corrode and spread, and will cause great harm to the patient; for when something biting is put on the syfac, it irritates it. 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt. 
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness does not come except because of the medicine that was put on it, so that its virtue may have effect, then it is fitting that you take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and in glue one cloth, and place it on the ulcer; then cure it in the manner that is fitting until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, for they are two bones; and that below is cartilaginous, and does not break, only if it is forced to bend or twist, and then heals. 
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is fitting that you put your little finger or thumb on the nose, and place the break inside with your index finger, and in the pouch by pressing, until the nose returns according to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee, and the bone cannot come back into place, then you must put it equal to the head of a nail, a large point. 
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, you must do it otherwise and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscesses have calmed down, then apply bandages of linen cloths to the head of the knee, if the fracture is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind it on the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the holes of the knee. 
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some healers say that one should moisten the bandages with butter and change them each day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they are softened with a mixture of egg yolk and mill powder; then leave the bandage until the bone is strong and the cartilage hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes put goose feathers in place of bandages, and if the sheet is wrapped around it, and the fracture is held, and the patient blows on it among; now do what you see. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the nose while you are working on it, put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or a piece of diachylon.  
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not come, put plaster on top, made of sesame flour and frankincense powder, mixed with egg yolk, then put it on light bandages, and do not tie the nose; and if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments for this purpose, then sew up the wound, and treat it with things that promote healing and joining together, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with bandages, and put splints of linen, until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone 
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured below and there is no external wound, and the break is only slight and not broken in two, but merely indented, if the practitioner recognizes it lightly. 
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, then put your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the fracture inward, and adjust it with the other hand externally, and make it equal. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension in two parts, so that it becomes equal. 
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or fracture, then bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and then put cerate on the fractured jawbone and put two cloths over it; and put a large well-made star on the cloth, or a piece of leather equal in length and width according to the jawbone, and tie it above the muscles as you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods. 
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, unbind it on the third day, and then reset what has changed; and put a plaster on it, made from powder from the mill with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the cerote; and put light wool on top of the plaster. And if the plasters dry out and the patient's condition does not change, leave them as long as they are healed; many times they are healed in three weeks.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if boils come, treat them as we have said many times. 
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see that no piece of bone is removed; use suitable instruments for this. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with a knife according to your need. 
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, if the wound is large, sew it up and put on suitable plasters for it to generate flesh until it is healed. 
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks several times before the shoulder, and the break is according to three manners: either it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.  
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when the break is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the forceps is broken; and the other extends the neck toward the part; then put the break evenly at your command, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor unevenness. 
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round sphere of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, and make it thick according to your need; stretch and lift the force, and pull the sphere with your hand so that you align the fracture as it should be. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the bone out further because it comes in too tight, it is necessary that the patient lie often on his back and put a medium pillow under the shoulder, and push the ministers' shoulder down until the bone of the humerus is lifted. 
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then straighten the fracture according to your judgment, and if you find it broken, it is necessary that you split it up; and draw the pieces lightly together, and if the bone cannot join due to any swelling, apply it to one of the incisors that you have; but put this instrument under the humerus to keep it in place: 
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not grooved, and is as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and it has two heads, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, as is the break in the wound that you have made when you have treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, if the wound is small, or if you doubt a hot abscess, then apply the wound with cloths and bandages according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, soak the cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put it on. 
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cuts, is that you put on the bone the plaster made from flour from the mill and egg yolk, and put light wadding on top, and put a splint under the armpit, if you need it; then take a very large bandage a palm wide, then put the cloth double on the wadding and the plaster; then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down; and put the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage up the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the unhealthy armpit; and loosen from each side, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture properly, and you see clearly that the stick does not move on the broken bone, then leave it for a day, and when the ligatures become slack, tighten them; and let the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under his armpit when he sleeps, to raise the shoulder joint upwards; this will lighten the fracture by the relief of the shoulder, or you can tie his arm to his neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents occur, until twenty days have passed; then renew the plaster, if you see that he needs it, and remove it and leave it like that until he is restored; and it is restored at most in twenty-eight days, and less for some men. 
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder 
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It sometimes happens that the shoulder is broken or dislocated, and it is not known except by touch; if you arrange it according to the shape of the break, and set it according to its natural form in all the ways that you can; then put on the place powder from the mill with plenty of egg, and light bandages, and put a double cloth over it; then put on a broad and subtle splint, a little larger than the shoulder, and if under the splint there is any swelling anywhere on the shoulder, use linen bandages so that the splint lies evenly; and then bind it all together with a large and firm bandage so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the binding every day; and whenever it loosens, unbind it and put the splint equal again if it has gone out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in twenty days or twenty-five; and when this number is fulfilled, untie it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that is put back lightly. 
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out in front, and not below the heart, then lift it up, and the bone-setter, and do what we have said about breaking the strength of the breastbone to soothe a hot abscess. 
de la brisure dou pis	Of the breaking of the thigh  
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The thigh is rarely broken in the middle, but it happens seldom; but it often breaks at the top. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it slopes downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and a lack of breath, and all at once, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the hair vessels in the broken bone, and one can feel it well. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back, and he puts a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two sides with his hands, and subtly puts them equal in all the ways that he can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then he puts on plasters and bandages over the thin plaster of salt, or another light herb, and wraps it in a cloth, and ties it over the broken bone so that it does not move; and he turns the bandage around the back, and loosens it carefully, and checks each hour the binding, and if it softens, he loosens it; and if it is necessary to untie it, for corrosion or for itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then he hastens and unties it, and removes the plaster, and attends to what has come in a manner of cures; then he remolds the plaster, and removes it until it is healed.  
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs 
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs only comes from behind in their thick part, and especially inward, and they only break because they are slippery, and the patient feels it well on inquiry at two places. 
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put the break straight, as it should be.  
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on a plaster and bind it with a splint if you need to. 
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is inward sloping, then the patient feels great pain and pressure as well as pleurisy because the bone points the lining; and he breathes with difficulty and vomits a large amount of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients have put forth great effort on it.  
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the break outward. 
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, so that a hot abscess does not come, unless it has already come. 
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, heal it.  
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that one puts cupping glasses on the place to suck out phlegm, and it seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not draw superfluities to the place due to weakness. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the place with linen moistened in hot oil, and put bandages between the ribs to apply equal pressure around, then it is cured by a treatment of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.  
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone pointing through the cloth, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut open above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put something under the instrument to protect the spinal cord; and then one must carve the bone, and draw lightly, and then sew the two edges of the wound if it is large, and cure it with plasters until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put it on cloths moistened in rose oil and apply it to the place; and treat the place as is necessary for an abscess, and let it lie frequently on its side where it should be until it heals. 
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the neck 
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture comes to the bones of the neck, and so it happens that he bends; and also in the spine of the back.  
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, observe if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.  
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortally wounded in several ways, and if he moves them and feels well when they are pulled and pricked, know that the junction of the bone is safe, and that the patient will be cured, if care is given to him.  
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if it is healthy or not, see if its feet are softened, and if the accidents which are in its hands, and on its back comes windiness and discharge without will; and when one has turned it onto its stomach, there comes discharge without will. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is turned on his back and wishes to sit up, he cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal; if one does not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, the thing is lighter. 
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you consider if there is a heated abscess, then put rose oil or egg yolk oil on the spine until it is soothed; then apply a comforting and drying plaster, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed. 
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is broken, it is necessary to cover it with the heart; and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, then treat it with ointment containing char, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", put your left hand under the piece, and place it even with the other hand at your power, then apply plaster and bandage on top, if you need it; then remove it, and if there are any broken bones, do so again, and remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone 
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It sometimes happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it does happen, it will only cause a slight diminution at the head; and make it long, and decline to the buttock, and the patient will experience pain in the area, and numbness, and swelling where it is broken. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above it, as long as you are above the fracture; and know which is the fracture and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, then put it equal to the fracture, as long as it is in its natural shape. 
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it slopes inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of that fracture appears to you. 
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it equal, apply a plaster, then place a splint of wood or horn on top, and hold the fracture so that it does not move; and apply pressure below the ribs, as long as the ligature is equal. 
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if boils come, do not touch them until the boils are calmed, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the restoration and hold it as it should be, unless there is any bad incident; and this is the way. 
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breaking of the shoulder 
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, so you must restore it according to one of two methods: one of which is that you take a splint plain of medium thickness, according to this form: 
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with two ties, and raise them up, and place the patient upon a seat; then lay the broken arm upon the splint, as far as the armpit, and make a curve in the splint, and then lean it upon some heavy object or have an assistant extend it downward; then put your hands on the fracture so they are even together, until the fracture returns as it should. 
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one lays the patient upon his back, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two assistants that one should hold what is above the fracture with his hands, and the other should hold below at all the ligatures, and extend each to their part. 
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, extract the ligature below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the assistants to their respective parts. 
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put one ligature halfway below the armpit, and the other towards the elbow, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the elbow, it is necessary to put the ligature lightly, without effort, as long as the fracture is aligned on the arm, and on the elbow; then align the fracture as it should be, and extract it, if abscesses do not form. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses do form, do not extract it until 7 days, and put soaked linen in water and rose oil on it, until the abscesses are soothed; then extract it, and the manner of extracting it is that you put the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder support, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the sheet, and extract on the shoulder support, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.
