And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use splints, and put on the fracture a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint two finger-widths of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three finger-widths on each side; then strain upon the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter upon the fracture, more strongly and less widely. 
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the settling of the splints and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt a boil will form hot, leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the bandage every three days, so that itching does not swell or come to the place, or that numbness does not come to the limb because it is too tight. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said. 
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents come, do not untie it except after III days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion full of equal wool, and look every hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or that the ligaments are not softened; if it heals by the virtue of medicine, and give him the meat we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the meat is at first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be kept in place for forty days altogether; and then one should untie it and administer baths and remedies for dressings to straighten the place. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and constricted, it will remain untied for one day or two months. 
de la brisure du bras	Of the breaking of the arm  
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "fosciles," of which one is small, and it is the one that enters the pouch; and the other is large, and it is the one below, towards the little finger; by chance, only the large foscile breaks, or the small one, and by chance both together. 
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small foscile is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken together. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small foscile that is broken, then you must gently extend it a little, and set it equal. 
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is a large muscle, then it is necessary to restrain more strongly; and spread it on a cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little fingers lower than the other fingers, and have the patient crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the minister's arm below his hand, or to the lien, and another minister above.  
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the sights equal, according to its best form. 
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is any detached that you cannot grasp with the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a splint as we have said before. 
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a singular chapter; so take the cure.  
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration there arise boils, then glue a plaster made from rose oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; and bind the plaster on top subtly, until the boils subside. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the wax plaster, and apply a poultice of powdered mill with plenty of egg yolk; then place the splints, and let the splint at the fracture be stronger and a bit wider than the others; and know that it must have six splints or arms in various positions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones or two; and pull more tightly above the fracture than elsewhere, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages over the fracture be soft and damp, not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is tied be linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.  
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and the ligament after a few days. 
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accidents come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you bathe the limb with hot water, until the itching is soothed; and let the limb not be tightly bound at rest. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin the bandaging again, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones are loosened, and similar things, so direct it. 
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you are careful that the blood supply cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then it is necessary that you loosen it a bit and leave it so for a few days until the circulation returns, and then remove it.  
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happen to the patient, do not unbandage it until 20 days. 
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Where there is entorsion, then he can put his hands on his neck, and let his necks be equal, and beware of movement and relaxation, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and perhaps in XX days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues. 
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand 
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and as we have two come many breaks, and there comes but weeping many times. 
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it behooves that the sick person sit upright, and sits straight in front of him equally; then puts his hand on the cloth extended, and extends the ministering bones broken, and sets them equal to the mire, so long as they are well joined; and put the plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not come, then he puts a splint according to the quantity of the place; and be wrapped in one linen sheet.  
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the middle of the sole of the foot, make a sphere of rags, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken foot; then strain it with a long bandage, and let the star be of wool as large as the palm of the hand, and strain it as it should be. 
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is below, it behoves you to put a star above and another below on the sole, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and seal the tie between the two. 
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, set it equal as it should be; and bind it with the palm, and if you see fit, put a small straight star to raise the fracture, so that it does not move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index finger or one of the others, set it equal and tie it with the healthy finger that follows; or tie them all together in a I shape, holding it tight, or put a star on it, as you would on the thumb; and be careful in restoration and the arrangement of hot abscesses, and help those who come to them, as I have said. 
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh 
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see this well when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration consists in tying one ligature above the break, and another below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends their ligature to their respective portion equally; and this is when the break is between the bones. 
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the thigh, one of the ligatures should be towards the hip, and the other ligatures below the break.  
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, then the ligatures should be near the knee, and the extension below; then put the splints against the bone equally with both hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and bandages, provided abscesses do not appear.  
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down then return to your work and your care; the ligature is made in this way. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is fitting that you wrap it on the fracture with a bandage doubled two or three times, and leave the excess, then turn the leg until the heels reach the root of the thigh, and put one long thread between the thigh and the leg below the knee, and bring the end of the thread above; then turn the bandage on the leg and on the thigh, then place splints on the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then insert eight layers of cloth between the leg and the thigh to equalize the pressure, then begin to tie three or four twists on the fracture; and when you go above the fracture, tighten less; then take the two ends of the thread that you have put between the leg and the thigh, and tie them to the three splints that are above, then go back down to the end of the thread until you reach the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, until no abscess or swelling or other similar thing appears. 
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, and the bone is dislocated, and repositioned as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that are caught, then you should remove them if possible; and if not possible, then you should cut open the area, and extract forcefully; and treat as we have said, until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no matter how broken the thigh is so that one puts splints on it, as in the shoulder or arm; nevertheless, in this restoration done thus does not inconvenience the patient. 
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 10 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions. 
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the space below the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the space below the knee there are few fractures, but it bends many times. 
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is just a crack or a hole, and occurs at any wound, whether the wound is seen or unseen, this will be fine. 
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done by putting together what is broken to its due place as much as it can be assembled; then apply the plaster and put a round splint if you need it, and remove it as necessary, then observe all the arrangements we have mentioned for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and other similar things. Apply to each accident what suits it until it is healed. 
de la brisure de la jambe	of a leg fracture 
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that the leg has two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" and the other is called "foscile"; and all fractures occur as in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as for the arm, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg will be twisted in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, do so beforehand. 
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, there is great pain, and it is seen well; and turn below. 
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension and set it equal, and tie the splints equally; but however, if the break is bad and there are many pieces, the extension should be less and lighter; and adjust according to your skill. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have accomplished all your work, take two bandages of beech wood that can support the leg on one side and the other, and they should be as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap them in two layers both above and below, and tie them in the middle as well, and with this binding, the leg cannot lean to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should administer bandages shorter than the length of the leg, and if they are beech wood, they are put on the leg to prevent movement, and properly done so at the fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg to see if there is a hot abscess or another accident; and cure it until it is healed. 
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of bones at the foot 
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there does not come a break, but the bones of the foot sometimes come to a break and some must be set, and there is no strength except for assurance in several positions. 
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones of the foot are broken, and you see these bones rise upon one another, then put the patient's foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, and then place your foot on theirs, where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their places; then apply a plaster and bandages above, and place under the belly of the foot a small board two fingers thick, then straighten the foot, and after you have wrapped it in cloths, and other things as needed. 
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated. 
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the toes broken, then restore them as we have said for the toes of the hand; then put on the broken toe a splint according to the length of the toe, and let it be a finger wider, then put under the foot that board which I have mentioned, and bind it firmly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then put on each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and let it be lying on the top of the board below the belly of the foot, so that he holds it well. 
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and treat each case as it is fitting. 
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the wrist 
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, have her sit enlarged, then incline her to the side of her back, and let her be held from behind; then fill the woman's nature with cotton, as large as I can put it in; then raise the woman, and loosen her back little by little, and then the cotton will jump out, as far as it comes to the entrance of her nature, and the bone will return with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or so: the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of a lamb, tie a cane to its opening, and put the whole bladder into her nature; then blow into the cane until the bladder is inflated inside: her nature will restore the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for several days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the arm of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said about the bone of the hip; and these fractures are not hidden from one who applies his study and practice and understands my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture indicates to us in several ways the right path for restoration: understand then. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	For the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's neck and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or so wrapped up, and it will be healed quickly. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound 
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, just as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, so that the healings we have mentioned testify to this.  
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, if you have no other remedy, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or day, so that no abscess comes. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess does come, leave the restoration until a new day, until the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will bring about bad accidents. 
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent above the heart uncovered, it is fitting that you put it in place lightly with your hands, with little extension. 
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear to you to put it in place with your hands, then have this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight lengths, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this it is necessary that it be sharpened so that it impinges three or four, according to what one needs in each cure of a fracture; and let it be round and have a large point so that it does not bend at compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front and thick from the middle forward, like this: 
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," for which reason it is necessary that the curved head be placed on top of the exposed bone; and the end at once, as much as it returns, and be equalized one against the other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone as much as the instruments have power. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone as we have said, then cut with an instrument suitable for this, either an incisor or a saw, according to your ability; then scrape away what remains in the bone of sharpness and small splinters. 
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. 
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth in black stiptic wine, and cleanly if it is in summer; and do not put any cerate or anything else on the wound where there is oil, lest it cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the break; and many times foolish barbers have done this, and have brought death or corrosion upon the patient; and let the binding be gentler and softer than other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, it is not right to put splints on it; but wrap around, instead of splints, hard cloths, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the dressing on the wound is swollen, remove what you have put on it all together and apply a healing ointment, such as Tetrapharmacon and similar ones. 
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and sound. 
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be bandaged in such a way that the swelling goes down slightly. 
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day passes and it cannot heal but the swelling returns, know that there are small bone fragments; therefore, it is necessary to reopen the wound with a tent and remove all these loose fragments which cause this pain. 
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the site, or another manner of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it according to what he said in this chapter before.  
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not pull it at all, for many times death comes, but leave it until it decays; perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Burns that come from soldering.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They come many times after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps it cannot make the limbs perform their natural actions. 
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore if it is fresh: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others, so that you take none of these things, or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with egg white or with oil; and put them on the swelling in compresses, and bind it well, and do not untie it for any days; and then untie it, and begin another, until the swelling is removed; or you bind it on a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut it off above, and make the superfluity apparent; or you scrape it with a razor until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.  
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb after healing 
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and the limb remains weak and thin, it happens for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages and nourishment could not come to the limb; or because of too much movement, or movements that are too large, not done at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak. 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and soften his body, as long as the blood multiplies within him; and give him baths, joy, and leisure; then put pitch on the limb so that the pitch draws great nourishment to it, and often apply a hot compress, until nourishment reaches the limb; and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a crooked limb after health 
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function; so do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish ones have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and it brings great evils, and by chance death; nonetheless, if the dislocations and the tortures are fresh, it is fitting that they be softened with hot water, or softening herbs be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as daikon well made, and take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with grease of goose or oil of sesame, and make plaster upon it; or you take fat figs, and crush them with bran of rye, and similar medicines that soften the swelling. 
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the dislocation removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands. 
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be administered to the limb every hour. 
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the crookedness is old and hardened, as stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then it should be cut up to the bone, with a subtle sharp instrument lightly; and put caution and study into the cure. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations 
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury. 
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation comes to someone, if it is necessary now to bring it back to its original position.  
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the place swells, and by chance if one puts it back in its place; therefore, it is not necessary to move it when it is swollen: many times it brings on spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient healthy, then leave it alone until the abscess boils are appeased; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then soften it lightly, and treat each member as the cure comes into its place.  
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from the head to the feet. 
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It can happen that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are a little moved from their places, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang down towards the ground, and cut the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and he wraps his tongue with speech. 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by several arrangements. 
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete, you must reset it quickly, and do not delay; and in such a way that the assistants hold the head of the patient, and put the index finger of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other hand should be free, to put it equal; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he looks at the eye equally, as long as it returns to its place. 
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if returning it is difficult, even when the two jawbones are together, then apply hot ashes and oil, as long as they soften them slightly; do not delay in returning it, as we have said. 
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned equally, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, put soft cloths soaked in cerate made of rose oil and wax on top, then tie it lightly with soft bandages; let the patient sleep on their back, with their cheeks resting between two pillows, so that they do not move it to the right or left, nor strain to chew, but take light food, as long as the pains are gone, and the jaws are joined; and then eat what they want lightly, and do not bother to open their mouth to eat and drink, as long as the jaw is well joined and healed. 
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not returned to their positions, then fever and habitual headaches may occur, and possibly loosening of the bowels, and possibly vomiting pure bile. 
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is fatal; and many times people have died within nine days who experienced this. 
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be dislocated from within the continuity of the hip and thighbone, and it is dislocated sometimes downwards, and one feels it well. 
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on their back and extends their arms; and then presses the place with the hollow of their hand, and it will return; then put on a plaster and bandage it, and remove it; and the head which is towards the hip cannot be dislocated; if it does, and if it dislocates sometimes, then reset it in its place, as we have said; then put on the plaster and bandage it, and remove it; and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and likewise, the head of the shoulder is brought back when it is displaced from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder 
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one of which is that it dislocates at the part of the armpit below; and the second is at the part of the breast; and by chance it dislocates above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and often times it dislocates below towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, because for them it is dislocated quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it is dislocated with difficulty, and goes back with difficulty. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it sometimes happens that some men have a concussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this. 
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore it is fitting that you examine it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.  
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that a dislocation has occurred when the shoulder is pulled towards the armpit, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest diversity between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the armpit on the humerus the head of the shoulder, just as if it were a bone; and the patient cannot bring his hand back to its place, nor move in any way; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, unless it is hidden, for you will find it clearly at the humerus; and this kind of dislocation is not very difficult to reset, when it is new, or if the child is sick. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the practitioner lifts the patient's hand upward, then puts his thumbs under the armpit, and lifts the joint forcefully upwards to its place; and the practitioner lifts the hand, and extends it upward, then puts it downward. It will come back quickly.  
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in a few days afterward, then it is fitting that the patient be bathed in hot water; and let him be given a mollifying and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of altaea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be applied; then let the patient be laid on his back, and put under the shoulder a cloth of wool equal, not too soft nor too hard, then put the patient's heel upon the cloth, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the hand of the patient; and another minister hold the head of the patient so that it does not move down; this shoulder will return at once, and if you see that the resetting is according to this manner: and it is fitting that you make a man be present who is larger than the patient; and he shall stand straight toward the side, and put his shoulder under the shoulder of the patient, and lift the shoulder upward so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pulls the hand of the patient downward towards the belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he may hold something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return now. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting is also done in another way: and it is that one puts a long burning coal in the ground, whose head be as round as a pistol, and not too thick nor too thin; then it is put under the patient, but let him have cloths soaked with water above him, and the patient be standing on the long end of the wood; then his hand is extended down on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a coal of two arms in length and four fingers wide, which has a round head for moving under the shoulder according to this form:  
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie cloths under the head of the wood so that the wood does not burn the patient, then put it under the shoulder of the patient; and extend his arm on top of the wood, and tie the shoulder onto the wood, and the arm to the head of the hand, then put the arm on the rung of a wide ladder, and let his hand be extended down, and leave his body hanging from the other side: the joint will return now.  
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, no matter the way, it behooves you to put under the shoulder a sphere of equal wool, then apply the plaster prepared with powder from a mill, with incense and egg yolk, upon the whole shoulder and bind it, then strain it under the shoulder gently, and return the bandage upon the plaster, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus. 
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it behooves him to rest a little, as long as the limb is comforted, for it will heal more quickly; and then rest more afterwards for five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is forced out of place due to moisture that has come upon it, or for another reason, it behooves you to administer cauteries at three points, as it is set forth in the chapter on cauteries. 
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise his arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place. 
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocation which is towards the buttock and the breasts or behind, is made by a push and stretching of the hands, and it is administered to another place; and heal as long as it is sound. 
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes pain to the limb, and slowness in movement, let the patient bathe many times, until that pain is relieved, and returns to its first nature. 
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder blade.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder blade is dislocated at points, and at points returns; and if it is dislocated from all sides, even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not put back in place, because one sees it well and feels it well; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick cautery with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly. 
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joining is raised and cannot bend the arm nor touch his shoulder at all. 
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you soften it in such a way that abscesses may come, for if abscesses were to come, it would be harmful to bring it back; and by chance it cannot be brought back entirely, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by chance death may come. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration, if it is such that it can be brought back, is done by extending his hand with your two hands; and let his arms be spread out, and his hands so that they see according to the cautery, up and down, and push the joint at his knuckles together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.  
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he bends his hand to his hand, and strong from the root of the palm or the cost which is dislocated. 
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and let the one who administers extend the arm, and hold it so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide; and when he looks at the joint, join his hand to it, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint straight, until it returns; and when it is in place, put dry plaster on it with yolk of egg, and bind it straight, and hold the arm against the neck of the patient, and leave it for several days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not quite right, start again with the plaster and bandage, and leave it like this for several days, until it is firmly set; then untie it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset and it moves, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is eased; or you put a greasy sheep's wool on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and let him enter a bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint temperately, then put the wool back on, and then enter a bath again; and do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see that it returns to its position. 
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand 
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is lighter than the other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the flesh is swollen, or there comes a hot abscess. 
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the return is such that you put the sick hand on a table, and extend the ministers' hand, and look at it to make it equal, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes as much as it returns. Nevertheless, you must see if it is well in place; then put the sick person's back of their hand on a table for extension and return.  
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, put the sick person's back of their hand on the table, and have them put their hand on that appearance of the joint. 
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is good; but if not, apply soothing plasters to the abscess and leave it alone without restarting. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint will remain twisted; and do not harm the patient further than to let his hand become weak, and unable to grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; if there is no other remedy but to extract it with a cautery in this case, and perhaps nothing else will work. 
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then untie it and leave it as is.  
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then apply hot water and rub it until it is healed. 
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the shoulders of the hand 
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the shoulder of the hand is dislocated on every side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly; then set the shoulder and push the dislocation towards your pouches as much as it will go back, then support the head of the shoulder and bend it towards the part where it is separated; and leave it for two days, then put it straight that day; and bind it at night, as we have said, and unbind it during the day, and make it move, and bind it again at night; and do this often until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated on the other side. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the dislocation of the shoulder blade of the back 
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient. 
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the excretions leap forth without volition, and he cannot hold them, and many times some limb is softened, either both thighs or both arms or one. And many times the shoulder blade moves in four parts; that which moves at the back is called "gilbositez"; the cure is that you observe whether the gilbositez has come from childhood: if there is no cure nor healing at all. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or impacts or similar things, the ancient ways of healing spoke in great words, in which there is not much profit in all; but I have shortened it according to my intention and have formed instruments in various ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes to the breast beforehand, nothing is felt; and also that which comes straight on both sides, and one cannot cure except that which properly comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient be stretched out on his face in an equal place, and have a strain underneath him so that he does not bleed; then put one ember at the head into the earth round, and the other at the feet, and tie a strap under the patient's buttocks, and the other at the haunches, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers know the straps, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two embers; and they are well fastened, the ember as we have said, and the minister put his palms on the spine round, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board of three arm's lengths long and put it under the wall, and let the patient be on his side, and push the head of the board under the wall, then put the middle of the board on the spine; and put the minister's feet on the other end of the board, and press well until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it on the tourniquet that turns in the hand. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you place two fires at the head of the patient's body, one arm's length from the feet, and between each fire, above and below, a palm's space in length; and have in each fire a hole where the wheel runs, and let the fires be firmly in the earth so they do not move; and between each two fires have another fire turning, with which the wheels turn, and have in the two turnings two small fires of a palm's length to turn the wheel; and then tie the rope that is among the axles to the wheel towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other wheel, and each of the assistants turns his wheel for all the rope, and the master puts the spine straight as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is straightened, apply a drying plaster with plenty of egg, and then bandages, and then an splint made from a tablet three fingers long, which covers the place of the gibbosity and the part of the vertebrae that is healthy; then tie it with a rope as we have said, and use the patient with subtle nourishment until he is healed; and if anything comes up at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines along with the splint mentioned above; and sometimes administer a piece of lead, and sometimes an appearance arises in the back vertebrae of the back, and one thinks it is a dislocation; it is the bone that appears, for which one should not have any presumption: for it might bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocatons of the hip 
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come loose by dislocations, not like the other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and it is more often dislocated inside, and seldom dislocated in front or behind. 
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of this dislocation inside is that when you join the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee towards the fire; and there is often swelling of a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one in whom it comes out outside is that this accident is the opposite of those in front. 
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has it beforehand are these: if his leg is well aligned according to its build; however, he cannot bend his knee even halfway without pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and he withholds his urine, and his groin swells, and when he walks, he passes on his heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has it behind are these: he cannot extend his knee or bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and his groin is softened, and the head of his thigh is located below the ribs. 
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The resetting of this kind of dislocation is such that you consider whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, if there is no cure; and it is not fitting for him to have confidence. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And as for those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are four kinds of dislocations, hasten to return the joint, and extend it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; by chance it will return, and needs no other treatment. 
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.
