And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary that you prepare a strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with both hands or with a band tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand over it in such a way that he puts his hands under his armpits, then he binds it with a strong bandage on the thigh; and another holds the head of the bandage; and they extend up and down all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation returns as we have said, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to put care into its resemblance When the dislocation is in the hip, it is necessary that you turn the patient onto his healthy side, then place the bandage on the root of the thigh, and the place which is below the angle, then extend the bandage upward toward the angle, and toward the groin; then have another minister take hold of his arms, and embrace the thick part of the sick thigh, and extend it outward: it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong cord above on the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the afflicted leg be extended two hands longer than the others; then let it be hung from the top of a pole, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then command your assistant to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another assistant hang with the patient, who embraces the calf, for the joint will now return quickly. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is below, let the patient lie down as we have said for one who has stiffness, and tighten the cord on the afflicted leg properly, and on the foot also; then put two embers, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert one ember between the thighs of the patient in the shape of a “V”; and place cloths moistened with water around it so that it does not burn the patient, then let each assistant stretch towards him, and the one who is looking should put his hand equally to the dislocation. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on a table and press it together as we have said in the matter of dislocation, and lay the patient on his sound side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, it is fitting to extend the sick leg quickly, and according as I have said; and put the patient's mind on being on the sore angle, then press with the other hand, and stretch downward toward the knee. 
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is backward, it is not fitting to extend the sick leg downward, nor lift it from the ground, but rather it should be as if the hip were dislocated backward, as we have said about lying on both hips; and he should be on his face, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint at the table; and it will be right when the patient extends his legs, and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and put on a plaster, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three days or four, then unbind him, and put on the plaster again; and if you see that they are even, bind it as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind him, and let him walk gently until his limb is comfortable. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee 
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated according to three manners: that is to say, inwards and outwards, and behind; and it does not dislocate forwards. 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not bend at his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and draw between your thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee together; and another minister extends his foot, as long as the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he bends his leg at his thigh easily; and apply a plaster on it, and make air the leg at the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three days or four, then unbind it; and let the patient not trouble himself with walking, as long as the limb is strengthened. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at all, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed. 
de la dislocation dou talon	of a dislocation of the heel 
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes loosened, and sometimes dislocated entirely, both inside and out. 
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen and taut in front of the part where it is dislocated; if resetting is easy, the foot should be gently extended with one's hands when it is only loosened. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated entirely, you should have the patient sit upright and hold his leg firmly by the thigh, above the ankle; then pull the foot toward you with your right hand, and then to the left twice, then extend it upward, and thrust the foot upward nicely; and do this twice, as we have said, by thrusting and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, have the patient lie on his back on the ground and fix a strong stick firmly in the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around it so that he does not bruise the patient; then one assistant holds the thigh and another assistant extends the foot with his hands or with a ligature tied onto the ankle; then each assistant extends equally, and the stick is now placed between the patient's thighs to hold him down when extending; then apply the mirror equal to the dislocation with your hands and have another assistant hold the sound leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly. 
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is set in place, apply the plaster and bandages on top and bind them firmly, tying the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind so that the bindings are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bindings loosen, rebind them. Then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before this time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it behoves you to soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed. 
des dois	from the two 
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they must be carefully extended without effort, and this is an easy thing to do. 
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, you must have the patient sit on a flat surface or table straight upright, and put your foot on what appears of those joints, then press your foot firmly until it returns; and when it is even and nothing appears, place under the sole of the foot a two-legged table, then bind it firmly and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let him rest until it is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and of dislocation together 
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and you want to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it long, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow, do not dare; and use at the beginning soothing things for hot abscesses, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscesses come alive; and when the limb is in place, then administer soothing things for hot abscesses, and treat the wound as it should be, with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are broken off, remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into the way of fear, according to what I have said, for this is worth more according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and your body. 
Amen	Amen
